First Proof: Faith is Tasdiq from Its Opposite (Kufr)
Nasafi proves that iman is tasdiq by analyzing its opposite, kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the opposite relationship between faith and disbelief to prove that faith is essentially affirmation (tasdiq), not action.

Core Idea
Faith is defined by its opposite: denial is to faith as affirmation is to belief.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi presents a concise logical proof that faith (iman) is essentially affirmation (tasdiq). He begins by establishing that the opposite of faith is disbelief (kufr), and then defines disbelief as denial and rejection. Using the Quranic pairing of faith and disbelief, he argues that the only meaning compatible with the opposite relationship is that faith is affirmation. This lesson will walk through his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the short Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall argument.
2
Analyze the logical structure
Identify the premises: (a) opposite of iman is kufr, (b) kufr is takdhib and juhud, (c) by opposite, iman must be tasdiq. Note the Quranic citation as evidence.
The proof relies on the principle that opposites are defined in relation to each other.
3
Reflect on what is excluded
Notice that other meanings of kufr (like ingratitude) are said to be metaphorical. Similarly, iman cannot include actions in its essential definition; it is restricted to affirmation.
This contradicts those who claim iman includes deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن ضد الإيمان هو الكفر، والكفر هو التكذيب والجحود، وإن كان يسمى به غيره على المجاز فكذا الإيمان يحققه أن الله تعالى قابل الكفر بالإيمان فقال: فَمَن يَكْفُرْ بِالطَّاغُوتِ وَيُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ ثم المراد منها التكذيب والتصديق لا غير فدل أن الإيمان ذلك.
He verifies that the opposite of faith (al-iman) is disbelief (al-kufr), and disbelief is denial (al-takdhib) and rejection (al-juhud), even if other than it is called by it metaphorically. So likewise faith: He verifies that Allah Almighty paired disbelief with faith, saying: 'Whoever disbelieves in Taghut and believes in Allah' (al-Baqarah 2:256). Then the intent from them is denial and affirmation (al-tasdiq) only. So it indicated that faith is that.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a proof. It begins by establishing that the opposite of iman is kufr. It then defines kufr as takdhib (denial) and juhud (rejection), noting that other things may be called kufr metaphorically. By analogy, iman must be the opposite: tasdiq (affirmation). The author then cites Quran 2:256, where Allah pairs kufr and iman, and argues that the intended meanings are denial and affirmation respectively. Thus, iman is essentially tasdiq.

Key Terms
إيمان (iman)
كفر (kufr)
تكذيب (takdhib)
جحود (juhud)
تصديق (tasdiq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that iman includes outward actions or verbal confession in its essence.
Correction: Nasafi shows that the opposite of iman is kufr, and kufr is essentially denial. Therefore iman must be essentially affirmation (tasdiq). Actions, while necessary, are not part of the essence.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does the opposite of faith (kufr) consist of?
A) Disobedience and sin
B) Denial and rejection
C) Hypocrisy
D) Shirk

Key Takeaway
Faith is essentially affirmation (tasdiq) because its opposite, disbelief, is essentially denial (takdhib), as confirmed by the Quranic pairing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If iman is essentially tasdiq, the heart's affirmation of truth, then right now, is your heart truly affirming Allah's truth in every area of your life, or are you holding back something? What specific truth are you denying by your actions or inaction? Decide one thing you will affirm today with your whole heart, and act on it.
?
The opposite of iman is kufr, which is denial. In what subtle ways have you been denying Allah's authority or His promises in your daily choices? Name one area where you have been rejecting His guidance and commit to turning back to affirmation tonight.
?
Faith is not just a label; it is a reality that must be affirmed in the heart. If you had to stand before Allah right now, would He find your heart truly affirming His oneness and His message? What is missing? Start today by putting aside one doubt or excuse and deciding to believe fully.

Linguistic Proof: Iman is Tasdiq
Nasafi presents a linguistic proof that iman is tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the conventional meaning of a word in the Arabic language establishes that iman (faith) is exclusively tasdiq (affirmation), and why changing this meaning leads to the absurd consequence of invalidating language itself.

Core Idea
The language itself defines iman as tasdiq; tampering with meaning destroys communication.

In this passage, Nasafi presents a concise linguistic proof that iman must be understood as tasdiq. He appeals to the authority of the Arabic language and shows that any deviation from its conventional meaning leads to an absurd outcome—the nullification of language itself. This argument is foundational to the Maturidi position on the definition of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the original Arabic
Read the Arabic passage slowly, noting the key terms: أهل اللسان, التصديق, محال. Try to sense the logical flow from the statement of convention to the hypothetical consequence.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Understand the literal translation
Compare the literal translation with the Arabic. Ensure you grasp that Nasafi is making an appeal to the people of language—the native speakers—as the authority on word meaning.
3
Analyze the argument's structure
Identify the three logical steps: (1) premise: iman means tasdiq in Arabic, (2) consequence: changing it violates the understood meaning, (3) absurd result: if allowed, all language would be invalid. See how the argument uses reductio ad absurdum.
This structure is typical of kalam proofs.
4
Reflect on the misuse of language
Consider how this argument defends against arbitrary redefinitions of religious terms. Ask yourself: Why is it important that iman has a fixed meaning in the language?
This connects to the broader issue of defining faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الإيمان معروف أنه عند أهل اللسان التصديق لا غير فمن جعله لغير التصديق فقد صرف الاسم عن المفهوم في اللغة إلى غير المفهوم ولو جاز ذلك لجاز في كل اسم لغوي، وفيه إبطال اللسان وتعطيل اللغة وذلك محال.
He verifies that faith (al-iman) is known, according to the people of language (ahl al-lisan), to be affirmation (al-tasdiq) only. So whoever makes it for other than affirmation has turned the name from the understood meaning in the language to a non-understood meaning. And if that were permissible, it would be permissible for every linguistic name, and that would entail invalidation of the tongue and nullification of language, and that is impossible (muhal).
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic proof. It states that iman, among the people of the Arabic language, is conventionally understood as tasdiq only. Changing its meaning violates linguistic consistency and would render language useless.

Key Terms
أهل اللسان (ahl al-lisan)
تصديق (tasdiq)
مجاز (majaz)
مفهوم (mafhum)
محال (muhal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that the meaning of 'iman' can be changed or expanded based on personal opinion or theological preference.
Correction: Nasafi argues that the meaning is fixed by linguistic convention; changing it would logically destroy the entire language, which is impossible. Therefore, the conventional meaning must be preserved.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the consequence of allowing someone to change the meaning of 'iman' from tasdiq to something else?
A) It would only affect religious terms
B) It would be permissible for every linguistic name, leading to the invalidation of language
C) It would be a valid interpretation since language evolves
D) It would make the meaning clearer

Key Takeaway
In kalam, the conventional meaning of words in the Arabic language is a binding authority; altering a word's definition without evidence leads to logical absurdity and the destruction of language.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you use the word 'iman', do you mean exactly what the Arabic language intends—affirmation of the heart—or have you unconsciously added or subtracted elements to suit your comfort? How would your faith change if you were precise about that definition?
?
If you allowed yourself to redefine a key religious term to avoid a difficult obligation, what would stop you from redefining every term until the entire Shariah loses its meaning? Nasafi says that leads to 'invalidation of the tongue'—are you willing to accept that for the sake of your own convenience?
?
Think of a time you insisted on a personal interpretation of a Quranic word against the clear linguistic convention. Was your motive sincere or defensive? How would you respond now if someone showed you the authoritative meaning from ahl al-lisan?

Third Proof: Quran Distinguishes Iman from Deeds
Nasafi cites Quranic evidence that iman is distinct from righteous works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses multiple Quranic verses to argue that faith (iman) is distinct from deeds (a'mal) and that committing sins does not negate faith.

Core Idea
The Quran consistently separates iman from righteous works and addresses sinners as believers.

Nasafi presents a cumulative Quranic argument to establish that iman is tasdiq (affirmation) and does not include deeds. By examining verses where iman and works are listed separately, conditional commands, and addresses to sinners as believers, he shows that the Islamic understanding of faith is distinct from actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of verses
Nasafi uses three types of Quranic evidence: (1) verses that list iman alongside specific deeds separately, (2) conditional commands that presuppose iman is known, and (3) addresses to believers despite their sins.
This structure forms the backbone of the proof.
2
Examine the first category
Read verses like 9:18 where iman, prayer, and zakat are mentioned as distinct items. Notice that iman is not equated with these deeds.
Also note 18:107 and similar verses that pair 'amanu' with 'amili al-salihat'.
3
Examine the second category
Look at verses where Allah commands something and then says 'if you are believers.' For example, 8:1, 2:278, 3:139. The condition shows that iman is already understood.
If iman were unknown, the condition would be useless.
4
Examine the third category
Consider verses like 2:178 where Allah addresses believers as 'O you who have believed' despite them committing actions that necessitate legal punishments. This shows that sin does not remove the name of faith.
This directly refutes the claim that avoiding sins is part of iman.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that if iman included deeds or required avoiding sins, these Quranic usages would be meaningless. Therefore, iman is simply tasdiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يدل عليه أن الله تعالى فرق بين الإيمان وبين كل عباده بالاسم المعقول على ما فرق بين العبادات بالأسماء المعقول لها على ما قال: إِنَّمَا يَعْمُرُ مَسَاجِدَ اللَّهِ مَنْ آمَنَ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَأَقَامَ الصَّلَاةَ وَآتَى الزَّكَاةَ وكذا قال في مواضع: إِنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ وكذا أمر بغير شيء ثم قال: إِن كُنتُم مُّؤْمِنِينَ نحو قوله تعالى: وَأَصْلِحُوا ذَاتَ بَيْنِكُمْ الآية وقوله: وَذَرُوا مَا بَقِيَ مِنَ الرِّبَا وقوله: وَلَا تَهِنُوا وَلَا تَحْزَنُوا وَأَنتُمُ الْأَعْلَوْنَ إِن كُنتُم مُّؤْمِنِينَ ولو لم يكن الإيمان معروفًا عند كل منهم وما به ثبت الاسم لكان يكون ذلك شرطا غير مفيد. وكذا خاطب الله تعالى باسم الإيمان على ما ارتكبوا من المعاصي الموجبة للحدود الوارد فيها الوعيد من نحو قوله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْقِصَاصُ فِي الْقَتْلَى وغير ذلك من الآيات التي تلوناها في مسألة وعيد الفساق، ولو كان الإيمان اسما لغير التصديق أو كان اجتناب الكبائر أو مطلق المعاصي شرطا لثبوت الإيمان لم يكن لذلك معنى.
It indicates that Allah Almighty distinguished between faith and all His servants by the understood name, just as He distinguished between acts of worship by the names understood for them. He said: 'Only those who believe in Allah and the Last Day and establish prayer and give zakah shall maintain the mosques of Allah.' And likewise He said in places: 'Indeed those who believe and do righteous deeds.' And likewise He commanded something then said: 'If you are believers,' such as His saying: 'And make peace between yourselves' (the verse) and His saying: 'And leave what remains of usury' and His saying: 'Do not weaken and do not grieve, and you are the uppermost if you are believers.' And if faith were not known among each of them and that by which the name is established, then that would be a condition that is not useful. And likewise Allah Almighty addressed them with the name of faith (believers) while they had committed sins that necessitate legal punishments and contain threat, such as His saying: 'O you who have believed, prescribed for you is legal retribution for the murdered.' And other verses we have recited in the issue of the threat of sinners. And if faith were a name for other than affirmation, or if avoiding major sins or all sins were a condition for the establishment of faith, that would have no meaning.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Quran. It first notes that Allah distinguishes iman from works in verses like 9:18, where iman, prayer, and zakat are listed separately, and 18:107, where iman is mentioned before righteous deeds. Then it points to verses where Allah commands deeds conditionally upon iman: 'If you are believers, then do X' (e.g., 8:1, 2:278, 3:139). If iman were unknown, such conditions would be useless. Moreover, Allah addresses sinners as believers despite their sins (e.g., 2:178). Therefore, iman cannot include deeds or require avoiding sins; it is simply tasdiq.

Key Terms
عبادات (ibadat)
شرط (shart)
كبائر (kaba'ir)
معاصي (ma'asi)
وعيد (wa'id)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iman includes deeds by definition, so a person who sins may lose faith.
Correction: The Quran consistently separates iman from deeds and addresses sinners as believers, showing that iman is tasdiq distinct from actions.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi use Quran 2:178 ("O you who have believed, prescribed for you is legal retribution") in his argument?
A) To show that believers must avoid sins
B) To show that Allah calls sinners believers
C) To prove that faith requires works
D) To define legal retribution

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's proof shows that iman is tasdiq alone, not including deeds, because the Quran separates them and addresses sinners as believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you internally feel that your faith has diminished or vanished? How does this passage's teaching—that Allah addresses sinners as believers—challenge or comfort you? Will you let it strip away your despair or your excuse to sin casually?
?
You have likely heard that deeds are a part of faith. Now this passage from the Quran says otherwise. Which of your assumptions about your own salvation rests on your deeds? Are you willing to let go of that security and rely solely on the tasdiq of your heart? What would that change about how you live today?
?
If iman is simply affirmation, and not the sum of your prayers and charity, then what is the real state of your heart? Are you comfortable with Allah knowing that inner reality? Or do you hide behind a flurry of deeds? This lesson forces you to examine not just what you do, but who you truly are. What answer do you give?

Proof from Enemies: Faith is Tasdiq Alone
Nasafi cites Pharaoh and Jonah's people as evidence that iman is tasdiq, not deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the behavior of Allah's enemies at moments of punishment demonstrates that true faith (iman) is essentially internal affirmation (tasdiq), not external deeds.

Core Idea
Even Allah's enemies resort to tasdiq when facing death – proving faith is inner affirmation.

Nasafi presents an empirical proof from the behavior of disbelievers. When Pharaoh and the people of Yunus faced drowning and punishment, they did not offer ritual prayers or charity but simply affirmed their belief. This shows that the essence of iman is tasdiq, as they had no time for deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it draws evidence from the behavior of Allah's enemies when facing punishment.
The verse references are Surah Yunus 10:90 and Surah Ghafir 40:84.
2
Identify the key figures and their actions
Pharaoh said 'I believe' when drowning; the people of Yunus said 'We believe in Allah alone' when punishment came. These are acts of tasdiq alone, without any deeds.
3
Connect to the definition of iman
Reflect: Why does Nasafi use these examples? Because they show that when deeds are impossible (or absent), what remains is tasdiq. This proves that iman is essentially tasdiq.
This is a key argument in the Maturidi position that iman does not include deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على أن الإيمان اسم للتصديق دون الأعمال أن أعداء الله تعالى فزعوا عند معاينتهم العذاب والبأس إلى التصديق دون غيره من الأعمال نحو لما أدركه الغرق قال: آمَنتُ الآية وقول قوم يونس عليه السلام: آمَنَّا بِاللَّهِ وَحدَهُ
And the evidence that faith is a name for affirmation to the exclusion of deeds is that the enemies of Allah Almighty, when they witnessed the punishment and calamity, turned to affirmation to the exclusion of other deeds, such as when Pharaoh was overtaken by drowning, he said: 'I believe' (the verse) and the saying of the people of Yunus: 'We believe in Allah alone.'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the behavior of disbelievers. When facing divine punishment, enemies of Allah (Pharaoh and the people of Yunus) only expressed tasdiq (affirmation) without performing any good deeds. This shows that iman is essentially tasdiq, as they did not offer works but were considered believers in that moment.

Key Terms
فرعون (Pharaoh)
يونس (Yunus)
غرق (drowning)
عذاب (punishment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That faith (iman) is valid only when accompanied by righteous deeds, and without deeds it is not true faith.
Correction: Nasafi shows that even the worst sinners (Pharaoh and the people of Yunus) were considered to have faith when they merely affirmed, without performing any deeds. This proves that deeds are not part of the definition of iman.

Checkpoint

C) "I will do good deeds"
D) "I submit"

Key Takeaway
The evidence from enemies of Allah shows that iman is essentially tasdiq, as they resorted to affirmation alone when facing punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow with only your inner affirmation of faith, would you feel it is enough? What does your comfort with that question say about your actual belief?
?
The enemies of Allah resorted to tasdiq at the point of death. Are you living as if tasdiq alone will save you without the deeds that manifest it? Examine your life: where are you relying on mere words?

Fifth Proof: Allah's Address to Ibrahim (A.S.)
Nasafi uses two Quranic citations to argue that iman is tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic dialogue with Ibrahim demonstrates that iman is tasdiq (affirmation).

Core Idea
Iman is affirmation, as shown by Ibrahim's reply 'Yes' to Allah's question.

Nasafi now presents two Qur'anic proofs that establish iman as tasdiq. The first comes from the dialogue between Allah and Prophet Ibrahim, where Allah asks 'Have you not believed?' and Ibrahim responds 'Yes' — meaning he affirms the raising of the dead. The second proof is from a verse stating that faith only benefits if it comes before certain signs. Both emphasize internal conviction over external actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the Quranic verses and Nasafi's commentary settle in your mind.
The passage contains two separate proofs; notice how each one points to tasdiq.
2
Unpack the Ibrahim proof
Focus on the first proof: Allah's question to Ibrahim and Ibrahim's reply. How does Nasafi interpret 'believe' here?
Nasafi says the question means 'Do you not affirm my raising the dead?' — this directly links iman to affirmation.
3
Examine the second verse
Now consider the second Quranic citation: Surah al-An'am 6:158. What point does Nasafi derive from it?
The verse implies that faith must come before seeing certain signs; again, it is about belief that precedes external evidence.
4
Synthesize the lesson
Combine both proofs: they both show that iman is not about seeing or doing, but about affirming in the heart. How does this strengthen the definition of iman as tasdiq?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على ذلك قوله تعالى لإبراهيم عليه السلام: أَوَلَمْ تُؤْمِن قَالَ بَلَى أي أولم تصدق بإحيائي الموتى؟ وقوله تعالى: يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ آيَاتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَانُهَا لَوْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ مِن قَبْلُ
And the evidence for that is His saying to Ibrahim: 'Have you not believed?' He said: 'Yes,' meaning 'Have you not affirmed my raising the dead?' And His saying: 'The day when some of your Lord's signs come, no soul's faith will benefit it if it had not believed before.'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the story of Ibrahim. When Allah asked Ibrahim 'Have you not believed?' (أولم تؤمن), Ibrahim replied 'Yes' (بلى). Nasafi interprets 'believe' here as 'affirm the raising of the dead' (تصدق بإحيائي الموتى). This shows that iman is tasdiq. Additionally, Quran 6:158 indicates that faith is only beneficial if it comes before seeing certain signs, again emphasizing affirmation rather than deeds.

Key Terms

أولم تؤمن

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The question to Ibrahim implies that he had doubt about Allah's power.
Correction: Ibrahim's reply 'Yes' shows he already had firm belief; the question was to affirm his tasdiq, not to correct doubt.

Checkpoint

C) Do you not perform good deeds?
D) Do you not worship Me?

Key Takeaway
The Quranic dialogue with Ibrahim affirms that iman is the act of heartfelt affirmation, not merely external deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Quranic Address to Believers: Proof That Faith is Separate from Deeds
Nasafi uses the order in Quran 2:183 to argue that iman is prior to and separate from deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the order of Allah's address in the Quran proves that faith (iman) is distinct from the acts of worship commanded.

Core Idea
Allah calls them believers before commanding deeds—faith comes first, deeds are separate.

Nasafi presents a concise yet powerful proof from the Quran. He points out that Allah addresses people as 'believers' before obligating acts like fasting. This sequence reveals a key distinction: if faith itself included those deeds, the separate command would be unnecessary. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and Nasafi's argument
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its translation. Notice that Allah first says 'O you who have believed' and then commands fasting.
The verse is Surah al-Baqarah 2:183.
2
Understand the logical implication
Reflect on the order: the address precedes the command. If faith already included fasting, why would Allah command it separately? The sequence shows they are distinct.
This is a simple but strong logical point.
3
Recognize the refutation of identity claim
This passage refutes the view that iman and deeds are identical. The Quran itself distinguishes between believing and being commanded to act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل عليه أنه تعالى خاطب باسم المؤمنين ثم أوجب الأعمال على ما قال: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الصِّيَامُ كَمَا كُتِبَ عَلَى الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ
And the evidence for it is that He addressed them with the name of believers, then obligated deeds, as He said: 'O you who have believed, fasting is prescribed for you as it was prescribed for those before you.'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the order in the Quran. Allah first addresses the believers (يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا) and then commands them to fast. If iman itself included fasting, such a command would be redundant. The separate command shows that iman is distinct from the deeds commanded.

Key Terms
المؤمنين (al-mu'minun)
أوجب الأعمال (obligated deeds)
صيام (fasting)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That iman and deeds are identical; one cannot have faith without performing all commanded deeds.
Correction: The Quranic address in this verse shows that Allah addresses people as believers before commanding deeds, implying that faith is already present and distinct from the commanded actions.

Checkpoint

A) That believers must fast to have faith
B) That faith is separate from the commanded deeds
C) That fasting is part of faith
D) That only believers should fast

Key Takeaway
The Quranic address 'O you who have believed' before a command proves that faith is prior to and separate from the commanded action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson shows that faith is separate from deeds. Does your daily life reflect that you are secure in your faith, or are you constantly anxious that your actions are not enough? What is one area where you can trust Allah's address over your own performance?

The Proof from Desisting: Iman is Tasdiq Alone
Nasafi argues from Quran 8:38 that desisting from kufr suffices for forgiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses Quran 8:38 to prove that iman is only tasdiq and does not include all righteous deeds.

Core Idea
Desisting from disbelief suffices for forgiveness; iman is not all deeds.

Nasafi presents a concise logical argument grounded in the Quran. By analyzing Allah's promise to forgive disbelievers who merely desist from kufr, he shows that iman cannot encompass all acts of obedience. This lesson walks through that reasoning and its implications for defining faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and nasafi's argument
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the verse and the logical structure of the proof.
The verse is Surah al-Anfal 8:38.
2
Identify the key premise
Nasafi states that desisting from kufr is achieved through iman. This premise connects the verse to the definition of faith.
3
Understand the conditional argument
If iman included all deeds, desisting would require all acts of obedience. But the verse only requires desisting, so iman must be something less than all deeds.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Recognize that this proof establishes iman as tasdiq (affirmation) alone, without necessarily including actions.
This is a key Maturidi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على أنه تعالى قال في الكفرة: إِن يَنتَهُوا يُغْفَرْ لَهُم مَّا قَدْ سَلَفَ والانتهاء عن الكفر يكون بالإيمان ولو كانت الأعمال كلها إيماناً لم يكن المنتهى عن الكفر منتهياً عنه ما لم يأت بجميع الطاعات
And the evidence that He said concerning the disbelievers: 'If they desist, what has passed will be forgiven for them.' And desisting from disbelief is by faith. And if all deeds were faith, then the one who desists from disbelief would not have desisted unless he performed all acts of obedience.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a proof from Quran 8:38, where Allah promises forgiveness to disbelievers if they desist (from disbelief). Desisting from kufr is achieved through iman (tasdiq). If iman included all righteous deeds, then merely desisting from kufr would not be enough to be forgiven; one would have to perform all acts of obedience. But the verse only requires desisting, showing that iman is tasdiq alone.

Key Terms
انتهاء (desisting)
غفران (forgiveness)
طاعات (acts of obedience)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think forgiveness requires a person to perform all acts of obedience before being forgiven.
Correction: The verse shows that merely desisting from disbelief through faith is sufficient for forgiveness, contradicting the idea that all deeds are required.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, if iman were all deeds, what would be required for a disbeliever to be forgiven?
A) Only saying the shahada
B) Performing all acts of obedience
C) Desisting from disbelief
D) Repenting from sins

Key Takeaway
Quran 8:38 proves that iman is simply desisting from disbelief through tasdiq, not the sum of all good deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely more on your deeds or on the simple fact that you have turned to Allah in tasdiq? How does your heart react to the news that desisting alone brings forgiveness?
?
If iman is not your deeds, then why do you sometimes feel less of a believer when you fall into sin? How can you cultivate the certainty that your iman remains as long as you hold to tasdiq?
?
The verse promises forgiveness simply for desisting from kufr. Are you truly free from the spirit of kufr—such as arrogance or ingratitude—in your heart, or do you hold onto some residue? What would it mean to fully 'desist' today?

Faith is Tasdiq: Proofs from Crisis and Prophets
Opening rejection and first three Quranic proofs for iman = tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quranic verses about Pharaoh, the people of Yunus, and Prophet Ibrahim demonstrate that iman is essentially tasdiq (affirmation of the heart) and does not include good deeds.

Core Idea
Crisis reveals faith as tasdiq, not works.

Imam Nasafi begins his argument by rejecting the idea that iman includes works or requires avoiding sins. He then presents the first set of Quranic proofs: when faced with divine punishment, even the enemies of Allah instinctively turn to tasdiq, not to performing deeds. The verses of Pharaoh at drowning, the people of Yunus, and Allah’s question to Ibrahim all point to the same essential nature of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening rejection
Notice how Nasafi first refutes the claim that iman is for other than tasdiq or that avoiding sins is a condition. Understand the logical consequence he draws.
2
Examine the crisis proofs
Read the verses about Pharaoh and the people of Yunus. Observe that at the moment of terror, they only say 'I believe' – no works are mentioned. This shows tasdiq alone is iman.
3
Study the Ibrahim proof
Read Allah's question to Ibrahim: 'Did you not believe?' and his reply 'Yes'. Nasafi interprets 'believe' as 'affirm' (tasdiq) regarding the resurrection of the dead. This confirms that iman means tasdiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى باسم الإيمان على ما ارتكبوا من المعاصي الموجبة للحدود الوارد فيها الوعيد من نحو قوله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْقِصَاصُ فِي الْقَتْلَى (١) وغير ذلك من الآيات التي تلوناها في مسألة وعيد الفساق، ولو كان الإيمان اسما لغير التصديق أو كان اجتناب الكبائر أو مطلق المعاصي شرطًا لثبوت الإيمان لم يكن لذلك معنى.
والدليل على أن الإيمان اسم للتصديق دون الأعمال أن أعداء الله تعالى (فزعوا عند معاينتهم العذاب والبأس إلى التصديق دون غيره من الأعمال نحو لما أدركه الغرق قَالَ آمَنتُ ) (٣) الآية وقول قوم يونس عليه السلام : آمَنَّا بِاللَّهِ وَحْدَهُ (٤) والدليل على ذلك قوله تعالى لإبراهيم عليه السلام: أَوَلَمْ تُؤْمِن قَالَ بَلَى (٥) أي أولَمْ تصدق بإحيائي الموتى؟ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ آيَاتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَانُهَا لَوْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ مِن قَبْلُ ) (٣) والدليل عليه أنه تعالى خاطب باسم المؤمنين ثم () أوجب الأعمال على ما قال أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الصِّيَامَ كَمَا كُتِبَ عَلَى الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ (٩) والدليل على أنه تعالى قال في الكفرة إن يَنتَهُوا يُغْفَرْ لَهُم مَّا قَدْ سَلَفَ (١٠) والانتهاء عن الكفر يكون بالإيمان ولو كانت الأعمال كلها إيمانا لم يكن المنتهى عن الكفر منتهيا عنه ما لم يأت بجميع الطاعات. وإذا ثبت الانتهاء بالتصديق وحصلت له المغفرة عما سلف به دل أنه هو الإيمان.
He, exalted, by the name of faith concerning what they committed of sins necessitating the prescribed punishments, for which there is threat of punishment, such as His saying, exalted: 'O you who have believed, prescribed for you is retaliation in cases of murder' (1) and other verses that we recited in the issue of the threat against the wicked. And if faith were a name for other than affirmation (tasdiq), or if avoiding major sins or absolute sins were a condition for the establishment of faith, that would have no meaning.
And the evidence that faith (iman) is a name for affirmation (tasdiq) without works is that the enemies of Allah, exalted, (took fright at the time they witnessed the punishment and severity and turned to affirmation without other works), such as when the drowning overtook him, he said: 'I believe' (3) the verse, and the saying of the people of Yunus, peace be upon him: 'We believe in Allah alone' (4). And the evidence for that is His saying, exalted, to Ibrahim, peace be upon him: 'Did you not believe?' He said: 'Yes' (5), i.e., did you not affirm (tasdiq) my reviving the dead? And His saying, exalted: 'On the day when some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before' (6). And the evidence for it is that He, exalted, addressed by the name of believers, then He obligated works, as He said: 'O you who have believed, fasting is prescribed for you as it was prescribed for those before you' (9). And the evidence is that He, exalted, said concerning the disbelievers: 'If they desist, what is past will be forgiven them' (10). And desisting from disbelief is by faith. If all works were faith, the one who desists from disbelief would not have desisted unless he performed all acts of obedience. And when desisting by affirmation is established and forgiveness for what has passed occurs for him, it indicates that it (affirmation) is faith.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage presents multiple Quranic proofs to establish that iman (faith) is essentially tasdiq (belief/affirmation) and does not include the works of the limbs. It begins by rejecting the alternative view that iman might be something other than tasdiq, or that avoiding sins is a condition. Then it cites verses where people turn to tasdiq at moments of crisis: Pharaoh at drowning and the people of Yunus. Then it cites the verse where Ibrahim is asked 'Did you not believe?' meaning 'Did you not affirm?' Then the verse that belief after seeing signs is not beneficial. Then the address to believers followed by commands shows that faith precedes works. Finally, it argues from the verse that those who desist from kufr by iman are forgiven, which would not apply if faith required all works. This confirms that iman is tasdiq alone.

Key Terms
إيمان
تصديق
أعمال
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith is a combination of belief and good deeds; without deeds, iman is invalid.
Correction: Nasafi argues that even sinners are called 'believers' in the Quran, and at times of crisis only tasdiq is demanded, proving iman is essentially tasdiq alone.

Checkpoint
What do the stories of Pharaoh and the people of Yunus illustrate about the nature of iman?
A) Iman includes works
B) Iman is only tasdiq (affirmation)
C) Iman requires avoiding all sins
D) Iman is a verbal confession

Key Takeaway
Iman is essentially tasdiq (affirmation of the heart), as shown by Quranic examples where only tasdiq is present.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a crisis strikes you, do you instinctively fall back on your deeds or on your inner tasdiq? What does your automatic response reveal about what you truly believe iman is?
?
Pharaoh uttered 'I believe' only when drowning, but it did not save him. Are you waiting for a disaster to affirm your faith fully, or are you living in tasdiq right now? What concrete change will you make today to ensure your heart’s affirmation is alive before the crisis comes?
?
Allah asked Ibrahim, 'Did you not believe?' about His power to resurrect. Do you affirm that Allah can bring the dead to life not just as a doctrine but as a reality that shapes your hope and patience? If you truly believed it, how would it change your response to personal failures or losses?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
8 min
Faith is Tasdiq: Proofs from Signs, Address, and Forgiveness
Three further Quranic proofs that iman = tasdiq, not works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse about belief before seeing signs, the address 'O you who have believed' followed by commands, and the verse on forgiveness for desisting from kufr all confirm that iman is tasdiq and not works.

Core Idea
Faith precedes works and makes forgiveness possible.

Imam Nasafi continues his argument with three more proofs. The first shows that faith is only beneficial before seeing signs, implying it is tasdiq that precedes works. The second shows that Allah addresses believers with commands, meaning iman is established before obedience. The third proves that desisting from kufr through iman brings forgiveness, which would not be possible if iman required all good deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the sign verse proof
Read the verse: 'On the day when some signs come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before.' Understand that belief here must be tasdiq before seeing the sign, not works.
2
Examine the address proof
Notice that the Quran often says 'O you who have believed' and then commands an action. This shows that the name 'believers' is given before the command, so iman must be something other than the works commanded.
3
Analyze the forgiveness proof
Read the verse that those who desist from kufr will be forgiven. Nasafi argues that desisting from kufr is by iman (tasdiq), not by performing all good deeds. If iman included all works, forgiveness would require all acts of obedience, which is not the case.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Nasafi argues that forgiveness is granted simply by desisting from disbelief through tasdiq. Is your own hope of salvation truly anchored in the affirmation of your heart, or are you secretly relying on your good deeds to tip the scales? What one concrete step will you take today to strengthen that inner tasdiq?
?
The verse about the day when signs come warns that faith after seeing them will not benefit. This means that now, before those signs, your faith is precious and urgent. Have you been treating your iman as a casual belief, or as the decisive, life-altering reality that it is? Write down one way you will actively affirm your iman in the next hour.
?
If iman were all works, the disbeliever would have to perform every act of obedience before being forgiven—an impossibility. This shows that Allah's mercy is immediate upon tasdiq. Do you truly believe that your Lord's forgiveness is that close, or do you hold back, feeling unworthy? What would it mean for you to accept that forgiveness right now, without waiting for perfection?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner

Iman and Disbelief as Opposites
Nasafi proves that iman is what removes kufr, and vice versa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that iman and kufr are logical opposites, each defined by the absence of the other, as proven by Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Iman and disbelief are opposites: one leaves the other behind.

Nasafi presents a concise proof that iman and kufr are opposites. He cites two verses where leaving iman leads to kufr, and vice versa. This lesson unpacks the logic and its theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the two Quranic verses cited.
The verses explicitly contrast iman and kufr.
2
Understand the logical relationship
Nasafi argues that iman is what removes kufr, and kufr is what removes iman. Think of them as opposites where one's presence negates the other.
This is a mutual exclusion relationship.
3
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that iman and kufr can coexist. The verses prove otherwise.
The prophetic warning shows that following certain people can turn you back to kufr, implying you leave iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الله تعالى قال : إِن تُطِيعُوا فَرِيقًا مِّنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَبَ يَرُدُّوكُم بَعْدَ إِيمَانِكُمْ كَافِرِينَ وقال : أَكَفَرْتُم بَعدَ إِيمَانِكُمْ ) ثبت أن الإيمان هو الذي به ترك الكفر والكفر هو الذي به ترك الإيمان.
He verifies it: that Allah the Exalted said: 'If you obey a party of those who have been given the Scripture, they will turn you back, after your faith, to disbelievers' and said: 'You have disbelieved after your faith.' So it is established that faith is that by which disbelief is left, and disbelief is that by which faith is left.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a short proof that iman and kufr are opposites. Nasafi cites two Quranic verses where the opposite of iman is called kufr, and the transition from one to the other occurs by leaving one. Hence, iman is defined as the abandonment of kufr, and kufr as the abandonment of iman. This supports the idea that iman is a single thing (tasdiq) that when present, kufr is absent.

Key Terms
إيمان
كفر
ضد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iman and kufr can coexist in the same person.
Correction: The verses prove that when one enters kufr, they leave iman, and vice versa. They cannot coexist because they are opposites.

Checkpoint
According to the verses cited, what is the relationship between iman and kufr?
A) They are complementary
B) They are opposites defined by mutual negation
C) They are identical
D) Kufr leads to iman

Key Takeaway
Iman and disbelief are mutually exclusive opposites; the presence of one necessitates the absence of the other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If iman is that by which you leave disbelief, then what does your daily life show: are you actively leaving disbelief through your faith, or are you just assuming you have iman because you avoid major sins?
?
The Qur'an warns that obeying a party of the People of the Book can turn you back to disbelief after faith. Who or what in your life might be influencing you away from iman? Will you cut that influence today?
?
The lesson proves that iman and kufr cannot coexist. Yet do you sometimes feel that a part of you still clings to disbelief—maybe in doubts, arrogance, or love of sin? What step will you take tonight to actively leave that behind?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
5 min
Refuting the Inclusion of Works in the Definition of Faith
Nasafi refutes the views that faith includes works or that each work is a separate faith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why iman cannot include acts of worship, based on consensus and logical consequences.

Core Idea
Faith is established by belief alone, before any works.

Nasafi presents two possible definitions of iman that incorporate works, then refutes each with clear arguments. The first refutation relies on the consensus of Muslims that faith is verified by mere belief before any acts of worship. The second refutation draws an absurd consequence that would make every act change one's religion. This lesson unpacks both refutations to solidify the correct understanding of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation. Notice how Nasafi structures his refutation by first stating the two possible definitions.
The passage uses conditional statements 'if they say...' to present each view.
2
Examine the first refutation
Identify the argument against faith including all acts of worship. Nasafi invokes consensus (ijma) that faith is established by belief alone before any works.
This argument shows that the first definition contradicts the unanimous agreement of Muslims.
3
Examine the second refutation
Understand the absurd consequence of defining every act as a separate faith: it would imply multiple religions and changing faith with each action.
This reductio ad absurdum shows the impossibility of the second definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الإيمان إما أن يكون اسمًا للتصديق والإقرار والعبادات كلها أو يكون اسمًا لكل عمل فكل عمل إيمان على حدة (كما هو طاعة على حدة)(٤) وعبادة على حدة.
فإن قالوا بالأول قيل (٥) : ينبغي أن يزول الإيمان بزوال بعض الأعمال أو بزوالها كلها، وقد أجمع المسلمون على تحقيق اسم الإيمان وإثبات حكمه بمجرد الاعتقاد قبل وجود غيره من العبادات، فكان ذلك فاسدًا بإجماع المسلمين. وإن قالوا بالثاني. فينبغي أن تكون الأديان كثيرة ويكون المنتقل من عبادة منتقلاً من دين إلى دين، والقول به باطل.
He verifies it: that faith is either a name for affirmation (tasdiq), confession (iqrar), and all acts of worship, or it is a name for every act, so every act is a separate faith (as it is a separate obedience and a separate worship). If they say the first, it is said: faith should cease with the cessation of some works or with the cessation of all of them. And the Muslims have consensus on the verification of the name of faith and the establishment of its ruling by mere belief before the existence of other acts of worship. So that (the first view) is invalid by the consensus of the Muslims. And if they say the second, then there should be many religions, and the one who transfers from an act of worship would be transferring from one religion to another religion, and holding this is false.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a classification and refutation of two possible definitions of iman. Nasafi presents two possibilities: (1) iman includes tasdiq, iqrar, and all acts of worship, or (2) every act of worship is itself a separate iman. He refutes the first by the consensus of the Muslims that iman is established by mere belief before any acts of worship are performed. If iman included all works, it would cease with the cessation of any work, which contradicts the consensus. He refutes the second by an absurd consequence: if each act were an independent faith, then leaving one act for another would be akin to changing religions, which is clearly false. This confirms that iman is a single entity, namely tasdiq.

Key Terms
إقرار
عبادات
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iman is a collection of all good deeds including acts of worship.
Correction: Iman is established by belief alone, before any works, as proven by consensus; works are separate acts of obedience that do not constitute faith itself.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi refute the view that iman includes all acts of worship?
A) By consensus that iman is established by belief before worship
B) By showing that works are not commanded
C) By citing the Mu'tazilites
D) By dividing iman into parts

Key Takeaway
Faith is a single entity (tasdiq) established by belief alone, not a collection of works.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your faith is weak because you are not doing enough good deeds? How does this lesson’s confirmation that faith is established by mere belief before any works change your perspective? What might you need to focus on now?
?
If faith does not decrease by sin, what stops you from sinning freely? Let the answer come from your heart, not from what you know is correct. Does this lesson free you from the burden of perfection, or does it confront you with the reality of your intentions?
?
Consider someone who commits a major sin. According to this lesson, they still have faith. But how do you treat them? Do you suspect their faith? This lesson demands you examine your own attitude toward others’ sins.

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
5 min
Defining Iman: The Act of Tasdiq That Ends Kufr
Al-Nasafi proves that iman is precisely the act of tasdiq that ends kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi proves that iman is identical to the tasdiq that ends kufr, and how this refutes the Mu'tazilite position.

Core Idea
Iman is nothing other than the tasdiq that ends disbelief.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Maturidi theological work tackles a central debate: is iman (faith) simply inner affirmation (tasdiq), or does it include outward actions? The Mu'tazilites hold the latter view. Al-Nasafi counters by citing Quranic verses that link the end of disbelief with forgiveness, arguing that the very act that removes kufr—tasdiq—is itself iman. As you read, notice how he uses a conditional argument to establish this identity and then verifies it with scripture.

Guided Path
1
Understand the conditional argument
Read the first sentence: 'If it is established that the ending (of disbelief) is through tasdiq and forgiveness is obtained... this indicates that it is iman.' Grasp the logical flow: X (ending disbelief) is achieved by Y (tasdiq), and X leads to Z (forgiveness). Therefore Y is iman.
This is a straightforward implication: what causes the end of disbelief must be the essence of faith.
2
Recognize the refutation of Mu'tazila
The author states that this disproves the Mu'tazilite view. In their understanding, iman includes acts of obedience, and a sinner leaves iman without necessarily entering kufr. But the verse shows that the act ending kufr (tasdiq) alone secures forgiveness, undermining their position.
The Mu'tazilites would not agree that mere tasdiq suffices for forgiveness without good deeds.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Read the cited verses (Quran 3:100 and 3:106) in context. The author then deduces a reciprocal definition: iman is what leads to leaving kufr, and kufr is what leads to leaving iman. This reinforces that the defining act of iman is tasdiq, because it is what removes kufr.
The verses speak of being 'turned back after your iman' and 'disbelieving after your iman', showing that the two states are defined by each other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت الانتهاء بالتصديق وحصلت له المغفرة عما سلف به دل أنه هو الإيمان. وفيه إبطال قول المعتزلة فإن في الآية دليلاً أن ما ينتهي به الكفر تحصل به المغفرة ويكون من انتهى كفره أهلاً للمغفرة، وعندهم ليس كذلك. يحققه أن الله تعالى قال : إِن تُطِيعُوا فَرِيقًا مِّنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَبَ يَرُدُّوكُم بَعْدَ إِيمَنكُمْ وأَكَفَرْتُم بَعدَ إِيمَنِكُمْ ثبت أن الإيمان هو الذي به ترك الكفر والكفر هو الذي به ترك الإيمان.
If it is established that the ending (of disbelief) is through tasdiq (affirmation) and forgiveness is obtained for what came before, this indicates that it (tasdiq) is iman (faith). And in this is the invalidation of the Mu'tazilites' statement, for in the verse there is evidence that what ends kufr (disbelief) obtains forgiveness by it, and the one whose kufr has ended is deserving of forgiveness, but according to them it is not so. He verifies it: Allah most high said: {If you obey a party of those who were given the Scripture, they will turn you back after your iman} and {Do you disbelieve after your iman?} So it is established that iman is that by which kufr is left, and kufr is that by which iman is left.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is a proof that iman is identical with the act of tasdiq by which disbelief is ended. The author begins with a conditional: if the end of disbelief is through tasdiq and forgiveness is attained, then tasdiq itself is iman. He asserts that this invalidates the Mu'tazilite position, because the quoted Quranic verses show that the thing that ends kufr is the means of forgiveness. Since the Mu'tazilites hold that iman includes actions, and that one who commits a sin leaves iman (but not necessarily into kufr), they would not agree that simply ending disbelief by mental affirmation suffices for forgiveness without additional acts. The author then provides a verification: he cites the verses (Quran 3:100 and 3:106) which speak of being turned back after iman and of disbelieving after iman. From these he draws the principle that iman is that by which one leaves kufr, and kufr is that by which one leaves iman. This establishes a reciprocal relationship: the two are defined by each other, and the defining act for iman is tasdiq, since that is what removes kufr.

Key Terms
iman
tasdiq
kufr
Mu'tazila

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is circular because it assumes iman is tasdiq in order to prove it.
Correction: The argument does not assume that; it uses the Quranic linkage between tasdiq, forgiveness, and the end of kufr to conclude that tasdiq is the defining act of iman, based on the reciprocal relationship established in the verses.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the ending of disbelief through tasdiq indicate?
A) That iman includes many acts
B) That tasdiq itself is iman
C) That the Mu'tazilites are correct
D) That forgiveness depends on all good deeds

Key Takeaway
Iman is defined as the tasdiq that ends kufr, proven by the Quranic association of tasdiq with forgiveness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your iman is the tasdiq that ends kufr, or do you rely on your deeds to assure you of forgiveness? Examine your heart: is your affirmation of faith the decisive act that turns you from disbelief, as the verse describes?
?
If iman is precisely the tasdiq that ends kufr, then what does it mean for you to say 'I believe'? Have you ever considered that your daily sins might indicate a weakening of that tasdiq, or do you treat iman as a fixed label rather than the active end of disbelief?
?
The Mu'tazilites thought that good deeds are part of iman and that sinners are in a middle state. Are you, like them, secretly trusting in your actions to complete your faith, or do you submit wholly to the Quranic truth that tasdiq alone is the iman that brings forgiveness? What would change in your life if you truly internalized this?

Iman Is Not the Name of All Acts Individually
Al-Nasafi refutes two possibilities for iman including all acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why iman cannot include all acts of worship either as a composite set or as individual acts, based on consensus and logical argument.

Core Idea
Iman is not defined by acts; it is established by belief alone before any act.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi tackles a key theological question: does 'iman' (faith) include the performance of all acts of worship? He presents two extreme possibilities and refutes both using consensus and logical reasoning. The argument is crisp and decisive, reinforcing the Maturidi position that iman is essentially tasdiq (affirmation) in the heart, expressed by the tongue, and confirmed by belief, independent of specific acts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two options
Read the Arabic passage. Notice that al-Nasafi presents two ways iman could include acts: either as a name for the combination of tasdiq, iqrar, and all acts, or as a name for every individual act.
These are the two extreme positions he will refute.
2
Analyze the first refutation
If iman were the composite, losing any part would negate iman. The Muslim consensus that iman is confirmed by mere belief before acts disproves this.
Consensus (ijma') is a strong proof here.
3
Analyze the second refutation
If every act were individually iman, then changing from one act to another would mean changing religion. This is absurd.
This shows the logical contradiction of the second option.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Al-Nasafi concludes that iman cannot include acts in either sense. Iman is essentially inner belief and verbal confession, not dependent on performing acts of worship.
This aligns with the Maturidi definition of iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الإيمان إما أن يكون اسمًا للتصديق والإقرار والعبادات كلها أو يكون اسمًا لكل عمل فكل عمل إيمان على حدة كما هو طاعة على حدة وعبادة على حدة. فإن قالوا بالأول قيل : ينبغي أن يزول الإيمان بزوال بعض الأعمال أو بزوالها كلها، وقد أجمع المسلمون على تحقيق اسم الإيمان وإثبات حكمه بمجرد الاعتقاد قبل وجود غيره من العبادات، فكان ذلك فاسدًا بإجماع المسلمين. وإن قالوا بالثاني. فينبغي أن تكون الأديان كثيرة ويكون المنتقل من عبادة منتقلاً من دين إلى دين، والقول به باطل.
He verifies it: iman is either a name for tasdiq, iqrar (verbal confession), and all acts of worship, or it is a name for every single act, so every act is iman individually, as it is obedience individually and worship individually. If they say the first, it is said: iman should cease with the ceasing of some acts or with the ceasing of all of them, yet the Muslims have unanimously agreed upon the realization of the name of iman and the establishment of its ruling by mere i'tiqad (belief) before the existence of other acts of worship; therefore that (the first option) is invalid by the consensus of the Muslims. And if they say the second, then religions should be many, and the one who transfers from one act of worship would be transferring from one religion to another, and that statement is false.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage presents a disjunctive argument and refutation. The author first states two possible interpretations of iman if it is taken to include acts: either (1) iman is a name for the combination of tasdiq, iqrar, and all acts of worship, or (2) iman is a name for each individual act, so that every act is itself iman. He then refutes both. Against the first: if iman is the totality of these, then losing any part should negate iman entirely. But the Muslim community (the Salaf and majority) has always affirmed that a person is called a believer by virtue of mere belief (i'tiqad) before performing any other acts. Thus the first option contradicts consensus and is invalid. Against the second: if every act of worship is itself iman, then each act would constitute a separate religion; moving from one act to another (e.g., from prayer to fasting) would be moving from one religion to another, which is absurd. Therefore, iman cannot be understood as including acts in either way.

Key Terms
iman
tasdiq
iqrar
i'tiqad
ijma'
Acts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that including acts in the definition of iman is consistent with Islamic teachings.
Correction: The passage shows that both ways of including acts lead to contradictions and are refuted by consensus and logic. Iman is established by belief alone before acts.

Checkpoint
Why is the first option (iman as a name for tasdiq, iqrar, and all acts) rejected?
A) It would make the term 'iman' meaningless
B) It contradicts the consensus that iman is established by mere belief before acts
C) It leads to multiple religions
D) It was never held by any school

Key Takeaway
Iman is not a composite of acts nor each act individually; it is fundamentally inner belief and verbal confession, established before any outward worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If iman is established by mere belief, according to the consensus cited, do you ever doubt the reality of your own iman when you fall short in acts of worship? How would holding onto this truth change your view of yourself before Allah?
?
The passage refutes the idea that each act is a separate religion. Yet do you sometimes treat one act—like prayer or charity—as the measure of your entire faith? How can you realign your heart to see acts as expressions of iman rather than its definition?
?
Since iman is fundamentally inner belief and confession, not a checklist of deeds, what does this demand from you in terms of sincerity and reliance on Allah's mercy? Will you let this lesson free you from despair over imperfect deeds, or will you use it as an excuse for complacency? What concrete change will you make today?

Iman's Missing Name: A Linguistic Proof
Al-Nasafi argues that iman lacks a specific name among acts, proving it is not an act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Nasafi's linguistic argument that the absence of a unique name for iman among acts of worship proves it is not an act of worship like prayer or fasting.

Core Idea
Iman has no unique name among acts — because it is not an act.

Al-Nasafi presents a clever argument based on the naming of acts of worship. Each act like prayer and fasting has a distinct name, but the supposedly highest act, iman, does not. This anomaly suggests that iman is not an act of worship at all, but a specific inner act of tasdiq. Let's examine the passage closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the repeated pattern of specific names for acts.
2
Identify the pattern for acts of worship
The author states that Allah has given each act of worship a specific name beyond the generic term 'ibada. For example, salat, sawm, zakat, hajj. Recognize this pattern.
3
Spot the anomaly for iman
Ask: if iman is the highest act, why does it lack a specific name? The author points out that people have never known a specific name for iman; they only know it as a name for a specific act (tasdiq).
This is the key point of the argument.
4
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that iman cannot be an act of worship like the others because it does not share the same naming pattern. It is a distinct act (tasdiq) that stands apart.
Refer back to the earlier established point that iman is tasdiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه : أن الله تعالى جعل لكل عبادة من العبادات اسما خاصا وراء اسم الجملة وهي العبادة فتكون هذه صلاة وتلك صومًا وزكاة وحجًا وغير ذلك، فما بال أرفع العبادات ليس له اسم خاص يعرف به خاصيته لا يشاركه فيه غيره، بل الناس لم تزل لا يعرفون له اسم الخاصية ويعرفون أنه اسم لفعل مخصوص على ما قررنا.
He verifies it: Allah most high has assigned to every act of worship a specific name beyond the general name 'worship', so this one is prayer, that one fasting, zakat, hajj, and others. So what is the matter with the highest of acts of worship that it does not have a specific name by which its particularity is known, which no other shares? Rather, people have never ceased not to know for it a name of particularity, and they know that it is a name for a specific act, as we have established.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is an argument from the nomenclature of acts of worship. The author points out that each act of worship (salat, sawm, zakat, hajj, etc.) has a unique name that distinguishes it from others under the generic term 'ibada. However, the supposed highest act—iman—does not have such a unique name; people simply call it 'iman' which is a name for a specific act (tasdiq). He argues that this would be anomalous if iman were itself an act of worship: the highest act would be the one most deserving of a distinct name, yet it lacks one. Thus, iman is not an act of worship like the others; rather, it is a specific act (tasdiq) that stands apart. The phrase 'as we have established' refers to earlier proofs that iman is only tasdiq.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'iman' is the generic name for all good deeds or acts of worship.
Correction: The author shows that each act of worship has its own specific name (salat, sawm, etc.), and iman itself has no such specific name, indicating it is not an act of worship but a specific act (tasdiq).

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The absence of a unique name for iman among acts of worship indicates that iman is not an act of worship but a specific inner act of tasdiq.

?
The highest act of worship lacks a specific name. Does your heart tremble at the thought that your iman might be unrecognizable as any outward action? How will you nurture it today so that it is not just a word but a transformative inner truth?

The Hadith of Jibril Proves Iman Is Only Tasdiq
Al-Nasafi uses the Prophet's answer to Jibril as definitive proof that iman is just tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Hadith of Jibril proves that iman is solely tasdiq (heartfelt affirmation) and why including actions would lead to absurd consequences.

Core Idea
The Prophet's answer to Jibril shows iman is only tasdiq, nothing more.

The Hadith of Jibril is a foundational text in Islamic theology, particularly for defining iman. In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents a compelling argument from this hadith to demonstrate that iman is nothing but tasdiq (affirmation of the heart). By examining the Prophet's response and the implications of adding extra components, we see a clear logical proof. Let's explore this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the Prophet's answer only mentions tasdiq.
The hadith text is summarized.
2
Understand the three consequences
The author lists three problems if iman included actions: Jibril would confuse, the Prophet would be deficient, and the Prophet's 'yes' would be a lie.
Each consequence is a separate logical point.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Realize that iman is only tasdiq, and the Hadith of Jibril is a decisive proof.
This is a key Maturidi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن النبي عليه السلام لما سأله جبريل عليه السلام عن الإيمان ما أجاب عنه إلا بالتصديق حيث قال: 'أن تؤمن بالله وملائكته' الخ.. لم يذكر فيه إلا التصديق ثم قال: هذا جبريل أتاكم يعلمكم أمر دينكم ولو كان الإيمان اسما لما وراء التصديق لكان إيتاؤه ليلبس عليهم أمر دينهم لا ليعلمهم، وكان النبي عليه السلام قد قصر في الجواب، وكان قول النبي نعم بعد قول جبريل 'فإذا فعلت هذا فأنا مؤمن' كذبًا والقول بعد كفر.
He verifies it: when the Prophet, peace be upon him, was asked by Jibril, peace be upon him, about iman, he did not answer him except with tasdiq, where he said: 'You believe in Allah, His angels, etc.' He did not mention in it except tasdiq. Then he said: 'This is Jibril, he came to you to teach you the matter of your religion.' And if iman were a name for what is beyond tasdiq, then his coming would be to confuse them about their religion, not to teach them; and the Prophet, peace be upon him, would have been deficient in the answer; and the statement of the Prophet 'yes' after Jibril's statement 'When I do this, I am a believer' would be a lie, and that statement would be disbelief.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the well-known hadith of Jibril. The author argues that the Prophet defined iman exclusively as tasdiq (affirmation of the heart) when asked directly, adding nothing else. After giving the answer, the Prophet informed the companions that Jibril had come to teach them their religion. The author reasons: if iman had included more than tasdiq (i.e., acts of worship), then the Prophet's answering only with tasdiq would have been misleading—Jibril would have come to confuse them rather than teach. Moreover, the Prophet would have been deficient in his answer, failing to mention the other components. Finally, if after performing these acts of tasdiq, Jibril were to ask 'When I do this, am I a believer?' and the Prophet said 'yes,' that would be false if iman required additional acts; such a response would be a lie, which is impossible for a prophet. Thus, iman is only tasdiq.

Key Terms
iman
tasdiq
Jibril
hadith
prophet

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that the hadith mentions 'belief in Allah, angels, etc.' which includes actions.
Correction: The author notes that these are all mental affirmations, not physical acts.

Checkpoint
According to the argument from the hadith of Jibril, what would be the consequence if iman included acts beyond tasdiq?
A) The Prophet's answer would be complete
B) Jibril would be teaching confusion
C) The companions would not understand
D) The hadith would be unreliable

Key Takeaway
The Hadith of Jibril decisively proves that iman is only tasdiq, as any other interpretation would lead to absurd consequences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Knowing that the Prophet's confirmation would have been a lie if iman included actions, how does this truth challenge your own definition of faith? Will you let this lesson reshape how you assess your own iman, not by deeds but by conviction?

Iman Is a Condition for Good Deeds, Not the Deeds Themselves
Al-Nasafi cites a hadith and a Quranic verse to show iman is distinct from actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why iman must be distinct from righteous deeds, based on prophetic hadith and Quranic reasoning.

Core Idea
Iman is a prerequisite for good deeds, not the deeds themselves.

This passage from Al-Nasafi uses two scriptural evidences to establish a crucial doctrinal point: iman (faith) is not identical to righteous actions; rather, it is a condition for their acceptance. The Prophet's listing of 'best deeds' distinguishes iman from jihad and hajj, and a Quranic verse makes iman a condition for reward. Let's see how the author builds his case.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage presents two distinct proofs.
2
Identify the hadith proof
The Prophet lists iman without doubt, jihad without deceit, and hajj mabrur. Notice why this distinguishes iman from actions. If iman were all good deeds, it couldn't be free of doubt because no one is certain of having all deeds. Also, the separate mention shows they are distinct categories.
3
Understand the Quranic proof
The verse makes iman a condition for righteous deeds. The author argues that if iman were the same as deeds, it would be a self-conditioning, which is impossible. A condition cannot be identical to that which it conditions.
4
Reflect on the logical argument
Consider why the author concludes that iman must be separate from all actions. This separation is fundamental in Maturidi theology for understanding the relationship between faith and works.
This distinction preserves the integrity of faith as a distinct inner state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدل على ما روى عن النبي عليه السلام أنه مثل عن أفضل الأعمال فقال: إيمان لا شك فيه، وجهاد لا غلول فيه، وحج مبرور ولو كان الإيمان اسمًا لكل الخيرات لا يجوز وجوده بلا شك لأنه لا أحد يقطع القول بإثبات جميع الخيرات، ولأنه غاير بين الإيمان وبين الغزو والحج وذلك دليل أنهما غير الإيمان، والدليل عليه أن الله تعالى جعل الإيمان شرطًا لقيام الأعمال الصالحة بقوله تعالى: فَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِنَ الصَّالِحَاتِ وَهُوَ مُؤْمِنٌ فَلَا كُفَرَانَ لِسَعْيِهِ ولو كان الإيمان اسمًا لجميع الأعمال الصالحة والخيرات لكان شرط الشيء وما به قيامه هو ذلك الشيء وهو محال.
And there is evidence for what has been related from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he gave an example of the best deeds, saying: 'Iman without any doubt, jihad without deceit, and hajj mabrur (accepted).' And if iman were a name for all good deeds, it would not be valid that it exists without doubt because no one can categorically assert the attainment of all good deeds; and because he distinguished between iman and ghazw (military expedition) and hajj, which indicates that they are other than iman. And the evidence for it is that Allah most high made iman a condition for the establishment of righteous deeds by His saying: {So whoever does righteous deeds while he is a believer, there will be no denial of his effort.} And if iman were a name for all righteous deeds and good things, then the condition for a thing and that by which it stands would be that same thing, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage presents two connected proofs. First, a hadith in which the Prophet enumerates the best deeds: iman free from doubt, jihad without deceit, and accepted hajj. The author argues: if iman were a name for all good deeds, then mentioning iman separately from jihad and hajj would be redundant; the distinction shows iman is a separate thing. Moreover, if iman included all good deeds, then one could never be certain of having iman, since no one can be sure they have performed all good deeds—yet the Prophet described an 'iman without doubt', indicating that iman itself can be certain. Second, the Quranic verse (21:94) makes 'iman' a condition for righteous deeds to be rewarded. The author reasons: if iman were identical to the set of righteous deeds, then the condition (iman) would be the same as the conditioned (righteous deeds), resulting in circularity (the thing conditioning itself). This is logically impossible. Therefore, iman must be distinct from all righteous deeds, serving as a prerequisite rather than the deeds themselves.

Key Terms
iman
jihad
hajj
shart
righteous deeds

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the hadith listing 'iman without doubt' among good deeds means iman is just one good deed among many.
Correction: The author shows that iman is mentioned separately and can exist without doubt, whereas other good deeds cannot be collectively ensured. Thus iman is a distinct category—a condition—not merely another deed.

Checkpoint
What logical problem does the author highlight if iman were the same as righteous deeds?
A) It would make reward impossible
B) The condition would be the same as the conditioned, which is impossible
C) The hadith would be contradictory
D) The Quranic verse would be meaningless

Key Takeaway
Iman is a condition for the validity of righteous deeds, not the deeds themselves; this is proven by prophetic listing and Quranic conditioning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly know that your iman is present and certain before you perform any good deed, or do you rely on the deeds themselves to give you assurance? What will you change tonight to prioritize the state of your heart over the actions of your limbs?
?
The Prophet praised 'iman without doubt.' In your own life, what doubts about your faith linger unaddressed? This lesson insists that iman can be certain even if your deeds are incomplete. Are you actively seeking that certainty, or do you ignore your doubts?
?
If your greatest deeds are worthless without iman, what are you doing daily to nurture your iman independently of your routine acts of worship? Examine your last week: how much time did you spend strengthening your belief vs. checking off religious tasks? When will you start the change?
