Iman is Essentially Tasdiq: Evidence from Hadith and Qur'an
The author argues that iman is tasdiq using prophetic hadith and Qur'anic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence that iman (faith) is essentially tasdiq (affirmation) and not a name for all good deeds.

Core Idea
Iman is tasdiq, not a collection of deeds—this is proven by prophetic and Qur'anic evidence.

The author presents a tightly reasoned argument that iman is specifically tasdiq, not a comprehensive term for all virtuous actions. Through the famous hadith of Jibril, a hadith about the best deeds, and a Qur'anic verse, he demonstrates that iman is a condition for deeds, not the deeds themselves. This lesson unpacks each proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the logical flow of arguments. The author first states his claim, then provides four distinct proofs.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Examine the first proof: Hadith of Jibril
The Prophet defined iman as tasdiq when asked by Jibril. If iman were more, the Prophet's answer would confuse rather than teach.
This is the primary evidence.
3
Examine the second and third proofs
The second proof is that the Prophet's 'yes' to Jibril's question would be false if iman included more. The third proof is the hadith distinguishing iman from jihad and hajj.
These show iman is distinct from other deeds.
4
Analyze the fourth proof: Qur'anic verse
The verse makes iman a condition for accepting deeds. If iman were those deeds, it would be a condition of itself—impossible.
This is a strong rational argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الناس لم تزل لا يعرفون له اسم الخاصية ويعرفون أنه اسم لفعل مخصوص على ما قررنا. يحققه أن النبي عليه السلام لما سأله جبريل عليه السلام عن الإيمان ما أجاب عنه إلا بالتصديق حيث قال: 'أن تؤمن بالله وملائكته...' لم يذكر فيه إلا التصديق ثم قال: 'هذا جبريل أتاكم يعلمكم أمر دينكم' ولو كان الإيمان اسما لما وراء التصديق لكان إيتاؤه ليلبس عليهم أمر دينهم لا ليعلمهم، وكان النبي عليه السلام قد قصر في الجواب، وكان قول النبي نعم بعد قول جبريل 'فإذا فعلت هذا فأنا مؤمن' كذبًا والقول بعد كفر، ويدل على ما روى عن النبي عليه السلام أنه مثل عن أفضل الأعمال فقال: إيمان لا شك فيه، وجهاد لا غلول فيه، وحج مبرور ولو كان الإيمان اسمًا لكل الخيرات [؟] لا يجوز [؟] وجوده بلا شك لأنه لا أحد يقطع القول بإثبات جميع الخيرات، ولأنه غاير بين الإيمان وبين الغزو والحج وذلك دليل أنهما غير الإيمان، والدليل عليه أن الله تعالى جعل الإيمان شرطًا لقيام الأعمال الصالحة بقوله تعالى: {فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِنَ الصَّالِحَاتِ وَهُوَ مُؤْمِنٌ فَلَا كُفْرَانَ لِسَعْيِهِ} ولو كان الإيمان اسمًا لجميع الأعمال الصالحة والخيرات لكان شرط الشيء وما به قيامه هو ذلك الشيء وهو محال. وفي المسألة دلائل كثيرة أعرضنا عن ذكرها تحاميا عن الإطالة.
People have never ceased to not know for it a name of specificity, and they know that it is a name for a specific action according to what we established. What verifies it is that the Prophet (peace be upon him), when Jibril (peace be upon him) asked him about al-iman, did not answer him except with al-tasdiq, where he said: 'That you believe in Allah, His angels...' He mentioned only al-tasdiq. Then he said: 'This is Jibril, he came to teach you your religion.' And if iman were a name for something beyond al-tasdiq, his bringing it would have confused them about their religion, not taught them. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) would have fallen short in the answer. And the Prophet's saying 'yes' after Jibril's saying 'If I do this, am I a believer?' would be a lie, and that statement is disbelief. And it is indicated by what is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he gave an example of the best deeds and said: 'Faith without doubt, jihad without deceit, and an accepted hajj.' And if iman were a name for all good deeds, it would not be possible [؟] its existence without doubt, because no one can categorically affirm the performance of all good deeds. And because he differentiated between iman and raiding (ghazw) and hajj, and that is evidence that they are other than iman. And the evidence for it is that Allah Almighty made iman a condition for the validity of righteous deeds by His statement: {So whoever does righteous deeds while he is a believer, there is no denial of his effort}. And if iman were a name for all righteous deeds and good deeds, then the condition of a thing and that by which it stands would be that very thing, which is impossible. And there are many proofs in the matter which we have omitted for fear of prolixity.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a proof that iman (faith) is essentially tasdiq (affirmation/assent) and not a name for all good deeds. The author begins by stating that people have always known that 'iman' is a name for a specific act, not everything. He then provides evidence: First, the hadith of Jibril: when Jibril asked the Prophet about iman, the Prophet answered only with tasdiq by mentioning the articles of faith. If iman were more than that, the Prophet's answer would have been confusing. Second, the Prophet's response 'yes' to Jibril's question about being a believer after doing certain acts would be false if iman included those acts. Third, another hadith listing best deeds: iman, jihad, hajj; they are distinct, so iman is not the same as those deeds. Fourth, the Qur'anic verse making iman a condition for accepting good deeds; if iman were all good deeds, it would be condition of itself, which is impossible. The author concludes that there are many other proofs but he omits them for brevity.

Misconception: Some think iman includes all good deeds and virtuous actions.
Correction: The author shows that iman is specifically tasdiq, and it is a condition for good deeds, not identical to them.

B) The verse about prayer

D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Iman is essentially tasdiq; it is not a name for all good deeds but a condition for them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Or do you sometimes perform deeds mechanically, without the core of tasdiq? What would change if you prioritized strengthening your iman as tasdiq before your actions?
?
The Prophet's answer to Jibril was exclusively tasdiq. If you were asked today 'what is iman?', would your answer align with the Prophetic model? What might that reveal about your understanding of faith?
?
The verse {فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِنَ الصَّالِحَاتِ وَهُوَ مُؤْمِنٌ} makes iman a condition for deeds. Consider your best deeds: are they accompanied by a firm, unwavering tasdiq? If not, what step will you take today to strengthen that inner affirmation?

Faith and Disbelief

Refuting the Claim that 'Iman' in the Verse Means Prayer
The author refutes the opponents' interpretation of the verse about prayer being called iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the verse 'Allah would not waste your iman' does not prove that prayer is part of iman, and why the term is used metaphorically.

Core Idea
The verse uses 'iman' metaphorically for prayer; the reality of iman remains tasdiq.

The opponents cite a verse to argue that prayer is called iman, implying it is part of faith. The author of Tabsirat al-Adilla refutes this by offering multiple interpretations and showing that the naming is metaphorical. In this lesson, we will examine his argument and see how he upholds the position that iman is solely tasdiq.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Familiarize yourself with the Arabic text and its literal meaning. Pay attention to the key terms.
The Arabic uses technical terms like tasdiq and majaz.
2
Identify the opponents' claim
What do the opponents cling to from the verse? They claim that 'iman' means prayer, implying prayer is part of faith.
3
Understand the three possible interpretations
The author enumerates three interpretations: 1) tasdiq regarding prayer's validity, 2) metaphorical naming because iman is a condition, 3) naming because prayer indicates iman.
Note that only the second interpretation involves metaphor directly.
4
Grasp the evidence from the hadith and Hanafi ruling
The author cites the report 'between a servant and disbelief is abandoning prayer' and the ruling that a disbeliever who prays is judged Muslim. This shows prayer is not iman but an indication.
5
Recognize the metaphorical nature and conclusion
By consensus, no single act is called iman in a way that abandoning it means leaving iman. Therefore, the verse's use is metaphorical, and the reality of iman is tasdiq.
This ties back to the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مناقشة قول الخصوم وإبطاله أنها ولا شبهة للخصوم فيما يتعلقون به من قوله تعالى {وَمَا كَانَ اللهُ لِيُضِيعَ إِيمَنكُمْ} أي صلاتكم إلى بيت المقدس، لأن الآية يحتمل أن كان المراد بها تصديقهم تكون الصلاة جائزة عند التوجه إلى بيت المقدس أو الواجب فيها هو التوجه إليه والإيمان هو التصديق. ويحتمل أن المراد بها الصلاة نفسها غير سميت إيمانا مجازاً لما أنها لا تصلح بدون الإيمان، فكان الإيمان شرط جوازها وسبب قبولها فسميت به مجازاً. ويحتمل أنها سميت إيمانًا لدلالتها على الإيمان إذ هي دلالة على كون مؤديها مؤمنًا، وقد ورد الخبر أن بين العبد وبين الكفر ترك الصلاة ولهذا قال علماؤنا - رحمهم الله - إن الكافر إذا صلى بجماعة كصلاتنا حكم بإسلامه والدليل على ذلك أن الصلاة بدون التصديق لم تكن إيمانا والتصديق بدونها إيمان حتى إن من صدق ثم مات من ساعته قبل توجه فرض الصلاة عليه لقى الله تعالى وهو مؤمن، فدل أنها كانت إيمانا باعتبار التصديق، إما لكونها دلالة عليه وإما لكونه شرطًا أو سببًا لها على أن الاسم محمول على المجاز بالإجماع فإنهم لا يجعلون الإيمان اسما لكل فرد من أفراد العبادات حق لا يكون الخارج عن الصلاة خارجا عن الإيمان ولا مفسدها مفسدًا للإيمان وكذا هذا في الصوم والحج وغير ذلك، ثم إطلاق اسم الجملة على كل فرد من الأفراد مجازاً فإذا كان الاسم مجازا كان حمله على ما ذكرنا أولى
Discussion of the opponents' statement and its refutation. There is no doubt for the opponents in what they cling to from His statement {And Allah would not waste your iman}, meaning your prayer towards Bayt al-Maqdis. Because the verse can be interpreted: it is possible that what is meant by it is their tasdiq that the prayer is permissible when facing Bayt al-Maqdis, or that the obligatory matter is facing it, and iman is tasdiq. And it is possible that what is meant by it is the prayer itself, except that it was named iman metaphorically because it is not valid without iman, so iman was a condition for its permissibility and a cause for its acceptance, so it was named after it metaphorically. And it is possible that it was named iman because it indicates iman, as it is an indication that the performer is a believer. And the report has come that between the servant and disbelief is the abandonment of prayer. For this reason our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) said: If a disbeliever prays in congregation like our prayer, he is judged to be a Muslim. And the evidence for that is that prayer without tasdiq is not iman, and tasdiq without it is iman, such that if someone affirms and then dies immediately before the obligation of prayer becomes binding on him, he meets Allah as a believer. So it indicates that prayer was iman by virtue of tasdiq, either because it is an indication of it or because it is a condition or cause for it. And the name is carried metaphorically by consensus, for they do not make iman a name for every individual act of worship such that the one who abandons prayer would abandon iman, nor the one who invalidates it would invalidate iman. Likewise in fasting, hajj, etc. Then applying the name of the whole to each individual is metaphorical. So if the name is metaphorical, it is more appropriate to apply it as we mentioned.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the opponents' argument that the verse {And Allah would not waste your iman} refers to prayer (salat) towards Bayt al-Maqdis, and thus iman includes prayer. The author explains that the verse can be interpreted in multiple ways. First, it could mean their tasdiq (affirmation) that the prayer is permissible or that facing Bayt al-Maqdis is obligatory. Second, it could mean the prayer itself has been metaphorically called iman because iman is a condition for its validity. Third, it could be called iman because it indicates the presence of iman. The author then supports his view with the report that abandoning prayer is not itself disbelief, but between a servant and disbelief is the abandonment of prayer, meaning that prayer is not part of iman but a sign. The Hanafi scholars rule that if a disbeliever prays like Muslims, he is considered Muslim, showing that prayer indicates iman but is not iman itself. The author emphasizes that the term 'iman' is applied metaphorically to individual acts, and by consensus, no single act is called iman in a way that abandoning it would be abandoning iman. Therefore, the metaphorical usage supports the author's position that iman is essentially tasdiq, not the acts.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse shows that prayer is part of the reality of iman.
Correction: The naming is metaphorical; prayer indicates iman but is not iman itself.

Checkpoint

B) Because iman is a condition for prayer
C) Because the Prophet said so
D) Because all acts are called iman

Key Takeaway
The verse does not prove that prayer is part of iman; the term is metaphorical, and the reality of iman remains tasdiq.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Does this knowledge make you more grateful for the opportunity to pray, or does it make you complacent? Refuting the Hadith: Narrator Doubt and Quranic Contradiction
Al-Nasafi criticizes the hadith's chain due to narrator doubt and its opposition to the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Nasafi rejects the hadith on branches of faith due to narrator doubt and contradiction with the Quran.

Core Idea
Narrator doubt undermines the hadith's reliability in creedal matters.

Imam al-Nasafi argues that the hadith on faith having many branches is invalid as a proof. He points out that the narrator himself expressed doubt about the number, which is unacceptable from the Prophet. Moreover, the hadith, being a solitary report, contradicts clear Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on narrator doubt
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the phrase where the narrator said 'sixty-odd or seventy-odd'. Notice the criticism of this doubt.
The author uses the term 'غفلة' (heedlessness) to describe the narrator.
2
Understand why doubt invalidates
Reflect on why a narrator's doubt is a problem: the Prophet (peace be upon him) cannot be uncertain, so the doubt reflects the narrator's own forgetfulness.
3
Learn the rule for solitary reports in creed
The author states that khabar al-wahid in creed must not contradict the Quran; here it does, so it is rejected.
This is a key principle of Maturidi kalam.
4
Connect to the bigger argument
Understand that this rejection clears the way for the author's position that actions are not part of iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا تعلقهم بالمروى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "الإيمان بضع وستون أو بضع وسبعون شعبة (۲) فاسد (۳) ، لأن الراوي شهد بغفلته حيث شك (فقال بضع وستون أو بضع وسبعون إذ لا يظن بالنبي عليه السلام الشك في ذلك) (٤) ثم التعلق بمثل هذه الأحاديث في (٩) باب الاعتقاد باطل لأن خبر الواحد لو لم يكن فيه دلالة غفلة الراوي ولم يكن ورد بمخالفة الكتاب فكيف وقد وجد فيه الأمران، أما دلالة الغفلة فلما ثبت فيه من الشك وأما مخالفة الكتاب فلما مر من دلائل القرآن على صحة ما ذهبنا إليه.
ثم المحتج بهذا الحديث يخالف الحديث) (٦) فإن في الحديث أن شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله شعبة من الإيمان وهو يجعلها إيمانًا، والأصل أن المتركب من أركان مختلفة لا يكون لكل ركن منه لا اسمه ولا حكمه كما في كل فعل من أفعال الصلاة وأفعال الحج وكالأنف أو الخد من الوجه والبياض أو السواد من الكف، وإذا جعل المتعلق بالحديث ذلك إيمانًا كان مخالفًا لما احتج به من الحديث على ما بينا أن الإيمان في الحقيقة هو التصديق لا يعرف أهل اللسان غير ذلك فإطلاقه على غيره يكون مجازا لكونه سببًا لقيامه في نفسه وشرطًا لصحته وثبوته، والله الموفق.
And likewise their clinging to what is narrated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'Faith has sixty-odd or seventy-odd branches' is invalid, because the narrator bears witness to his heedlessness when he doubted (saying 'sixty-odd or seventy-odd' since the Prophet, peace be upon him, cannot be thought to doubt about that). Then clinging to such hadiths in matters of belief is invalid, because if a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) does not contain an indication of the narrator's heedlessness and is not reported in opposition to the Book, how (can it be accepted) when both matters are found in it? As for the indication of heedlessness, it is because of the doubt established in it; and as for opposition to the Book, it is because of the proofs from the Qur'an that have passed on the correctness of what we hold. Moreover, the one who argues by this hadith contradicts the hadith itself. For in the hadith, the testimony that there is no god but Allah is a branch of faith, but he (the opponent) makes it faith itself. The principle is that something composed of different pillars cannot have for each pillar neither its name nor its ruling, as in every action of prayer and actions of pilgrimage, and like the nose or cheek from the face, and whiteness or blackness from the palm. And if the one who clings to the hadith makes that (testimony) faith, he contradicts what he argued from the hadith. Upon what we have explained: that faith in reality is affirmation (tasdiq), and the people of language do not know anything else. So applying it to other than that is metaphorical, because it is a cause for its establishment in oneself and a condition for its correctness and confirmation. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage refutes the opponents' use of the hadith that 'faith has sixty-odd or seventy-odd branches.' The author, Imam al-Nasafi, gives two main criticisms. First, the hadith is unreliable: the narrator himself doubted the number (saying 'awkward or seventy-odd'), which indicates heedlessness, and the Prophet cannot be thought to doubt. Also, the report is a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) that contradicts the clear Qur'anic proofs already presented, so it is invalid in matters of belief. Second, the opponents misunderstand the hadith: the hadith lists the testimony of faith as one branch, but the opponents treat it as the whole of faith. The author explains that in composite things, parts do not take the name or ruling of the whole (like actions of prayer do not get the name 'prayer' individually). Hence, calling the testimony 'faith' contradicts the same hadith. The author reiterates that faith in language is only tasdiq, and any other usage is metaphorical due to causation or condition. Thus, the hadith does not support the idea that actions are part of the reality of faith.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد
غفلة
شك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith on branches of faith is authentic and proves actions are part of iman.
Correction: The hadith is weak due to narrator doubt and contradicts the Quran, so it cannot be used as a proof in creed.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the narrator was heedless?
A) He forgot the number.
B) He doubted the number.
C) He rejected the hadith.
D) He changed the wording.

Key Takeaway
The hadith on faith's branches is unreliable due to narrator doubt and contradicts the Quran, so it cannot be used to prove actions are part of iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a hadith that seems to contradict a clear verse of the Quran, do you immediately question its authenticity, or do you try to reconcile them even if it means twisting the meaning of the Quran? How will you change your approach from today?
?
The narrator in this hadith showed doubt, yet many continue to use it as proof. Are there any beliefs or practices you hold that are based on doubtful or weak narrations? Will you examine them now with the same rigor as al-Nasafi?
?
This passage teaches that a solitary report cannot override the Quran in creedal matters. Is there an area of your faith where you have given more weight to a single narration than to the explicit Quran? What step will you take to realign your conviction with the primary source?

Internal Contradiction and the Definition of Faith
Al-Nasafi shows the opponent's inconsistency and defines iman as tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the opponents' interpretation of the hadith contradicts itself and that faith (iman) in language is only tasdiq (affirmation).

Core Idea
The hadith itself shows testimony is a branch, not the whole of faith.

Imam al-Nasafi continues by exposing an internal inconsistency: the opponents treat the testimony of faith (shahada) as the whole of iman, but the hadith lists it as just one branch. He then reaffirms that the true meaning of iman is tasdiq, and any other usage is metaphorical.

Guided Path
1
Locate the internal contradiction
Read the part where the author says the opponent contradicts the hadith: the hadith lists shahada as a branch, but the opponent makes it the whole iman.
The author uses a logical principle: parts of a composite do not take the name of the whole.
2
Understand the principle of parts vs. whole
The author gives examples from prayer, pilgrimage, and body parts to show that a part does not inherit the name or ruling of the composite.
This refutes the opponent's claim that a branch can be called iman in the same sense.
3
Grasp the linguistic argument
The author states that the people of language know only tasdiq as the meaning of iman. Applying it to actions is metaphorical, based on causation or condition.
This is the core of the Maturidi position that actions are not part of the reality of iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا تعلقهم بالمروى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "الإيمان بضع وستون أو بضع وسبعون شعبة (۲) فاسد (۳) ، لأن الراوي شهد بغفلته حيث شك (فقال بضع وستون أو بضع وسبعون إذ لا يظن بالنبي عليه السلام الشك في ذلك) (٤) ثم التعلق بمثل هذه الأحاديث في (٩) باب الاعتقاد باطل لأن خبر الواحد لو لم يكن فيه دلالة غفلة الراوي ولم يكن ورد بمخالفة الكتاب فكيف وقد وجد فيه الأمران، أما دلالة الغفلة فلما ثبت فيه من الشك وأما مخالفة الكتاب فلما مر من دلائل القرآن على صحة ما ذهبنا إليه.
ثم المحتج بهذا الحديث يخالف الحديث) (٦) فإن في الحديث أن شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله شعبة من الإيمان وهو يجعلها إيمانًا، والأصل أن المتركب من أركان مختلفة لا يكون لكل ركن منه لا اسمه ولا حكمه كما في كل فعل من أفعال الصلاة وأفعال الحج وكالأنف أو الخد من الوجه والبياض أو السواد من الكف، وإذا جعل المتعلق بالحديث ذلك إيمانًا كان مخالفًا لما احتج به من الحديث على ما بينا أن الإيمان في الحقيقة هو التصديق لا يعرف أهل اللسان غير ذلك فإطلاقه على غيره يكون مجازا لكونه سببًا لقيامه في نفسه وشرطًا لصحته وثبوته، والله الموفق.
And likewise their clinging to what is narrated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'Faith has sixty-odd or seventy-odd branches' is invalid, because the narrator bears witness to his heedlessness when he doubted (saying 'sixty-odd or seventy-odd' since the Prophet, peace be upon him, cannot be thought to doubt about that). Then clinging to such hadiths in matters of belief is invalid, because if a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) does not contain an indication of the narrator's heedlessness and is not reported in opposition to the Book, how (can it be accepted) when both matters are found in it? As for the indication of heedlessness, it is because of the doubt established in it; and as for opposition to the Book, it is because of the proofs from the Qur'an that have passed on the correctness of what we hold. Moreover, the one who argues by this hadith contradicts the hadith itself. For in the hadith, the testimony that there is no god but Allah is a branch of faith, but he (the opponent) makes it faith itself. The principle is that something composed of different pillars cannot have for each pillar neither its name nor its ruling, as in every action of prayer and actions of pilgrimage, and like the nose or cheek from the face, and whiteness or blackness from the palm. And if the one who clings to the hadith makes that (testimony) faith, he contradicts what he argued from the hadith. Upon what we have explained: that faith in reality is affirmation (tasdiq), and the people of language do not know anything else. So applying it to other than that is metaphorical, because it is a cause for its establishment in oneself and a condition for its correctness and confirmation. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage refutes the opponents' use of the hadith that 'faith has sixty-odd or seventy-odd branches.' The author, Imam al-Nasafi, gives two main criticisms. First, the hadith is unreliable: the narrator himself doubted the number (saying 'awkward or seventy-odd'), which indicates heedlessness, and the Prophet cannot be thought to doubt. Also, the report is a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) that contradicts the clear Qur'anic proofs already presented, so it is invalid in matters of belief. Second, the opponents misunderstand the hadith: the hadith lists the testimony of faith as one branch, but the opponents treat it as the whole of faith. The author explains that in composite things, parts do not take the name or ruling of the whole (like actions of prayer do not get the name 'prayer' individually). Hence, calling the testimony 'faith' contradicts the same hadith. The author reiterates that faith in language is only tasdiq, and any other usage is metaphorical due to causation or condition. Thus, the hadith does not support the idea that actions are part of the reality of faith.

Key Terms
إيمان
شعبة
مجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since the hadith calls the shahada a 'branch of iman', the shahada itself is iman.
Correction: The shahada is only a part; it does not constitute the whole iman, just as a nose is not the whole face.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the linguistic meaning of 'iman'?
A) Actions of the limbs.
B) Affirmation (tasdiq) of the heart.
C) Verbal confession.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
The hadith on branches of faith actually supports the view that actions are not part of iman, because the shahada is just a branch, and iman in language is only tasdiq.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite the shahada daily. But do you truly affirm it in your heart, or are you merely uttering a branch without the root? How would you know the difference, and what are you doing to ensure your iman is more than just words?
?
The opponent in this passage contradicted themselves by treating a branch as the whole. In your own life, have you ever equated an external action (like praying or fasting) with the entirety of your faith, neglecting the inner conviction? What would change if you prioritized tasdiq over outward show?
?
The author says iman in language is only tasdiq, and actions are metaphorical. Does this comfort you or challenge you? Are you relying on your deeds to save you, or on your affirmation of Allah? What one step can you take today to strengthen your tasdiq?

Refutation of the Karramiyya: Iman is Heart Affirmation, Not Just Speech
Quranic refutation of Karramiyya view on iman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Karramiyya claim that iman is merely speech is refuted by Quranic verses proving iman is an inner reality in the heart.

Core Idea
Iman is inner affirmation, not just outer words.

The Karramiyya sect claimed that iman (faith) is nothing more than verbal declaration. In this passage, the author directly refutes this claim by citing several Quranic verses that clearly tie iman to the heart, known only to Allah. As you read, pay close attention to how each verse serves as evidence against the Karramiyya position.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full English translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
The passage is a continuous refutation using multiple Quranic proofs.
2
Identify the Quranic proofs
List the four Quranic citations the author uses. For each, ask: how does this verse disprove the idea that iman is just speech?
Verses from Surah an-Nisa (4:25, 4:145) and Surah at-Tawbah (9:80, 9:54).
3
Understand the logical conclusion
The author ends by stating that anyone who calls a heart-denier a believer is corrupt in intellect and religion. Connect this to the definition of iman as tasdiq (affirmation).
Iman is defined as affirmation (tasdiq), not mere speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان إلا القول لكان كل سامع واحدًا ولم يكن لقوله: اللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِإِيمَانِهِنَّ معنى وقال: مِن فَتَيَاتِكُمُ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ ثم قال: (وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِإِيمَانِكُمْ) فكان دليل أن الإيمان حقيقة بالقلب حيث يعلم الله تعالى به، وكذا الله تعالى وعد المنافقين النار بل قال إنهم فِي الدَّرْكِ الْأَسْفَلِ مِنَ النَّارِ وهذا في من هو مؤمن حقا وليس بكافر كما يزعمه الكرامية محال، على أن الله تعالى شهد عليهم بالكفر بقوله: (اسْتَغْفِرْهُمْ أَوْ لَا تَسْتَغْفِرْ لَهُمْ إِن تَسْتَغْفِرْ لَهُمْ سَبْعِينَ مَرَةً فَلَن يَغْفِرَ اللهُ لَهُمْ ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُمْ كَفَرُوا بِاللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ) فمن زعم أن الله تعالى غالط في تسميتهم كفارًا بل هم مؤمنون حقا، لم يكن في كفره شك، وكذا قال تعالى: (وَمَا مَنَعَهُمْ أَن تُقْبَلَ مِنْهُمْ نَفَقَاتُهُمْ إِلَّا أَنَّهُمْ كَفَرُوا بِاللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ) وهذا أوضح من أن يحتاج فيه إلى الإطناب إذ من سمى المكذب بقلبه مؤمنًا مع أن الإيمان هو التصديق، لا يخفى فساد كلامه وسخافة عقله ورقة دينه على أحد، والله الموفق.
Faith is not just speech, for then every listener would be [the same] and His words 'Allah knows best their faith' would have no meaning. And He said: 'from your believing maids' then said: 'and Allah knows best your faith'. So that was evidence that faith is truly in the heart, as Allah Almighty knows it. Likewise, Allah Almighty promised the hypocrites the Fire, rather He said they are in the lowest depths of the Fire, and this is regarding one who is truly a believer and not a disbeliever, as the Karramiyya claim, is impossible. Moreover, Allah Almighty testified against them with disbelief by His words: 'Ask forgiveness for them or do not ask forgiveness for them; if you ask forgiveness for them seventy times, Allah will never forgive them; that is because they disbelieved in Allah and His Messenger.' So whoever claims that Allah Almighty was mistaken in calling them disbelievers when they are truly believers, there is no doubt about his disbelief. And likewise He said: 'And what prevented their contributions from being accepted except that they disbelieved in Allah and His Messenger.' This is too clear to need elaboration, for whoever calls one who denies in his heart a believer while faith is affirmation, the corruption of his speech, the weakness of his intellect, and the flimsiness of his religion are not hidden from anyone. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Karramiyya who claim that iman is merely verbal declaration. The author uses Quranic evidence to show that iman is in the heart. First, he quotes 4:25 where Allah says He knows the iman of the believing women, and 4:25 again (or similar) that Allah knows your iman, proving it is in the heart. Then he cites 4:145 about the hypocrites being in the lowest depth of the Fire, which would be impossible if they were actually believers as the Karramiyya claim. He also uses 9:80 and 9:54 to show that Allah calls the hypocrites disbelievers. If anyone says Allah made a mistake in calling them disbelievers, that person is himself a disbeliever. The author concludes that it is obvious that calling a denier in the heart a believer is corrupt, foolish, and weak in religion. Iman is tasdiq (affirmation), and the evidence is clear.

Correction: The Quran shows that iman is in the heart, known only to Allah. The hypocrites spoke faith but were disbelievers.

Worldly vs. Afterlife Judgments
Author distinguishes worldly and afterlife judgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Karramiyya confused speech with faith and how the author distinguishes worldly rulings from afterlife judgments.

Core Idea
Worldly rulings rely on appearances; afterlife judgments require true belief.

The Karramiyya argued that iman is merely verbal testimony because they observed that Islamic rulings in this world are based on speech. But this confuses two distinct domains: the worldly realm, where humans judge by what is apparent, and the afterlife, where Allah judges by inner conviction. In this passage, the author clarifies the correct boundaries of each domain.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the flow of the argument.
The author begins by describing the Karramiyya's reasoning.
2
Identify the two domains
The author distinguishes between worldly rulings and afterlife judgments. Find where each is mentioned and how they differ.
Worldly rulings are based on what can be seen; afterlife rulings are based on inner belief.
3
Understand the Karramiyya's mistake
The Karramiyya applied the principle of worldly judgments to the afterlife. Why is that a mistake?
The author says there is no argument about worldly rulings; the debate is about the afterlife.
4
Reflect on the key distinction
Consider how this distinction affects the definition of iman. Why must faith involve the heart, not just the tongue?

Source Text

وكأن هؤلاء ذهبوا إلى ذلك لما رأوا من إجراء أحكام الإسلام على الذين شهدوا باللسان، وهذا كهذا في حق إجراء الأحكام إذ لا اطلاع للعباد على الضمائر والعقائد فيكون الاعتبار في حقهم لما يمكنهم الوقوف عليه لما لم يمكنهم تعليقا للتكليف بما في الوسع ولا كلام فيه إنما الكلام في حق اعتباره في أحكام الآخرة التي تثبت في حق الله تعالى، والله الموفق.
It is as if these people went to that because they saw that the rulings of Islam are applied to those who testify with the tongue. And this is like that in terms of applying rulings, since servants have no access to consciences and beliefs; thus consideration for them is based on what they can ascertain, because they cannot attach obligation to what is beyond capacity. There is no argument about that; the argument is about considering it in the rulings of the afterlife, which are established in the right of Allah Almighty. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage explains the motivation behind the Karramiyya's error. They observed that in this world, Islamic rulings (like inheritance, marriage, etc.) are applied based on a person's verbal testimony of faith, because humans cannot see into hearts. The author notes that this is correct for worldly matters: rulings are based on what is apparent. However, the real issue is the afterlife, where judgments are based on true belief in the heart, not mere speech. The author distinguishes between the two domains, clarifying that the Karramiyya wrongly applied the worldly principle to the afterlife.

Two proofs that iman is in the heart
Two proofs that iman is in the heart: religion and act impossibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two rational arguments from the Maturidi tradition that establish iman as a matter of the heart, not merely the tongue.

Core Idea
Faith is in the heart, proven by its nature as religion and by its constant presence.

This passage from Imam Nasafi presents two proofs that iman is primarily a heart belief. The first proof is conceptual: iman is a religion, and religion is necessarily believed in the heart. The second proof is practical: the act of iman cannot be removed from a person even in situations where verbal expression is impossible, such as during prayer or in the toilet. Together, these arguments show that iman is inward affirmation, not outward speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice the two distinct proofs presented.
The passage uses the word 'يُحَقِّقُهُ' to introduce each proof.
2
Identify the first proof
The first proof states: 'iman is a religion, and religions are believed, and beliefs are in the hearts.' Reflect on why this connects iman to the heart.
This is a concise logical connection.
3
Understand the second proof
The second proof is longer. It argues that iman cannot be absent because it is always obligatory, even when speech is impossible (e.g., during prayer, in the latrine). Find these examples.
The author uses daily life situations to show that iman remains despite inability to speak.
4
Examine the Quranic support
The author cites verse 16:106 to support the argument. Notice how the verse shows that forced speech does not negate heart faith.
5
Confirm the conclusion
The passage concludes that the heart is the locus of iman, and disbelief in the heart prevents tongue speech from being faith. Summarize this in your own words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الإيمان دين والأديان تعتقد والاعتقادات بالقلوب. يحققه أن ارتفاع فعل الإيمان عن الممتحنين محال، وتمر عامة الأوقات ولا توجد الشهادة باللسان بل من الأحوال ما ينهي المرء فيه أن يقول آمنت بالكتب والنبيين والبعث ونحو ذلك كما في الصلوات وكما في حال كونه في الكنيف، وكما في حال خروج البول والغائط منه ومحال ارتفاع فرض الإيمان أو النهي عنه ما دام التكليف باقيًا أو القول بكراهيته حال وجود العبادة التي لا صحة لها إلا به، وكل ذلك يدل على أن الإيمان في الحقيقة هو التصديق، والذي يؤيد هذا كله قوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنٌّ بِالْإِيمَانِ﴾ لم يجعل لهم كفرًا باللسان إذا لم يكن عبارة عن القلب ومنع ذلك أن يكون كفرًا بإيمان القلب فثبت أن القلب هو موضع الإيمان وبه يستدل أن كفر القلب يمنع قول اللسان من أن يكون إيمانًا، والله الموفق.
It confirms that faith is a religion, and religions are believed, and beliefs are in the hearts. It confirms that the absence of the act of faith from those tested is impossible; most times pass and the testimony with the tongue is not present, rather there are situations in which a person is prohibited from saying 'I believe in the books, prophets, resurrection' and the like, as in prayers, and as in the state of being in the latrine, and as in the state of passing urine and stool from him. And it is impossible to remove the obligation of faith or forbid it as long as obligation remains, or to say that it is disliked in the presence of an act of worship that is only valid through it. All of that indicates that faith in reality is affirmation. And what supports all of this is His statement: 'Except one who is forced while his heart is assured in faith.' He did not make their tongue speech constitute disbelief if it is not an expression of the heart, and that prevented that from being disbelief due to the faith of the heart. So it is established that the heart is the locus of faith, and by it it is inferred that the disbelief of the heart prevents the speech of the tongue from being faith. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage contains two proofs. The first proof: 'iman is a religion, and religions are believed, and beliefs are in the hearts.' This establishes that iman, as a religion, is inherently a matter of heart belief. The second proof is more detailed: the act of iman cannot be raised from those who are tested (i.e., obligated). The author notes that most of the time, a person does not utter the shahada with the tongue; for instance, during prayer one cannot say 'I believe', nor while in the latrine, nor while passing urine or stool. Yet iman remains obligatory; it cannot be lifted or forbidden as long as the person is under obligation. Therefore, iman must be in the heart. The Quranic verse 16:106 supports this: the heart's assurance prevents the tongue's statement from being disbelief. Thus the heart is the locus of iman.

دين
اعتقاد
قلب
شهادة
تصديق

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that iman can be suspended or become non-obligatory in certain states (e.g., during prayer or in the toilet).
Correction: The author argues that iman is always obligatory and cannot be raised; its absence is impossible as long as one is under divine obligation. Even when verbal expression is forbidden, iman remains.

Iman is Tasdiq, Not Mere Knowledge: Refutation of Jahm
Al-Nasafī argues that iman is tasdiq, not ma'rifa, using opposition logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why iman is defined as tasdiq (affirmation) rather than mere knowledge (ma'rifa), based on the logical opposition between iman and kufr.

Core Idea
The opposite of iman is denial, not ignorance.

This passage from Tabṣirat al-Adilla tackles a fundamental question: What is the essence of iman? The author, al-Nasafī, refutes the view of Jahm ibn Ṣafwān that iman is merely knowledge. By examining the opposites of iman and disbelief, he demonstrates that iman must be affirmation (taṣdīq) in the heart, not simply knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the key terms: تصديق (affirmation), تكذيب (denial), معرفة (knowledge), and جهل (ignorance).
The passage is short but dense; read it twice.
2
Identify the main claim
The author asserts that iman is tasdiq (affirmation) and that knowledge without affirmation is not iman. This is his core thesis.
Contrast this with Jahm's view that iman is knowledge.
3
Follow the logical argument
The author argues: The opposite of iman is kufr. Kufr is takdhib (denial). Denial opposes tasdiq (affirmation), not knowledge. Therefore, iman must be tasdiq, not knowledge.
This is a classic opposition argument: if A opposes B, and A is the opposite of C, then C must be B.
4
Consider the counterexample
The author adds: Not everyone who is ignorant of a truth denies it. This shows that denial and ignorance are not opposites, further supporting that iman is tasdiq.
One can be ignorant without denying; denial requires active opposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بالقلب يكون التصديق لما مر أن الإيمان يكون بالقلب والإيمان هو التصديق، وليست المعرفة الخالية عن التصديق إيمانًا كما ظن جهم وجماعة أن الإيمان هو المعرفة لما أن الإيمان هو التصديق ثم ضد الإيمان هو الكفر، والكفر هو التكذيب والتكذيب ينافي التصديق لا المعرفة إذ ما يضادها النكرة والجهالة، وليس كل من جهل حقا يكذب به.
Then with the heart is affirmation, because it has been stated that faith is in the heart and faith is affirmation. And knowledge devoid of affirmation is not faith, as Jahm and a group thought that faith is knowledge, because faith is affirmation. Then the opposite of faith is disbelief, and disbelief is denial, and denial opposes affirmation, not knowledge, since what opposes it is ignorance and nescience. And not everyone who is ignorant of a truth denies it.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage refutes Jahm's view that iman is mere knowledge (ma'rifa). The author begins by reiterating that iman is tasdiq (affirmation) in the heart. He then argues that knowledge without affirmation is not iman. The key logical argument is: the opposite of iman is kufr (disbelief). Kufr is takdhib (denial). Denial is the opposite of tasdiq (affirmation). If iman were knowledge, its opposite would be jahl (ignorance), not denial. Therefore, iman must be tasdiq, not knowledge. Additionally, not everyone who is ignorant of a truth denies it; one can be ignorant but still not deny. This further shows that denial and knowledge are not direct opposites.

Misconception: Iman is simply knowledge (ma'rifa) of Allah, regardless of affirmation.
Correction: The author shows that denial (takdhib) is the opposite of iman, and denial opposes affirmation (tasdiq), not knowledge. Therefore iman must be affirmation, not mere knowledge.

B) Because denial (takdhib) opposes affirmation (tasdiq), not knowledge
C) Because Jahm said so
D) Because knowledge is in the heart

Key Takeaway
Iman is affirmation (tasdiq) in the heart, not mere knowledge; the opposite of iman is denial, not ignorance.

?

Proof that Iman is Tasdiq in the Heart
Nasafi proves iman is tasdiq in the heart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that true iman (faith) is inner affirmation (tasdiq) in the heart, not merely verbal confession.

Core Idea
Iman is not what you say but what settles in your heart.

In this passage, the Maturidi scholar Abu Hafs al-Nasafi presents a compelling case that iman is fundamentally a matter of the heart. He uses everyday examples and a powerful Quranic verse to show that verbal testimony cannot be the essence of faith because it is not always possible, while iman remains obligatory. Read on to see how he builds his proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic text and translation
Read the entire passage in Arabic and then the English translation. Notice the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the examples and the verse citation.
2
Identify the initial claim
Nasafi begins by stating that iman is a religion, and religions are believed in the heart. This sets the foundation.
3
Examine the practical proof
He argues that verbal testimony cannot be the essence of iman because there are situations where it is impossible to utter (e.g., during prayer or in the lavatory), yet iman must still be present.
Think about why these examples are effective.
4
Consider the Quranic evidence
Verse 16:106 shows that one compelled to utter disbelief retains iman if the heart is firm. This proves the heart is the locus of faith.
Note how the verse supports the conclusion.
5
Conclude with the key takeaway
Reflect on the conclusion: iman is tasdiq in the heart, and heart disbelief prevents verbal confession from being accepted as iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الإيمان دين والأديان تعتقد والاعتقادات بالقلوب. يحققه أن ارتفاع فعل الإيمان عن الممتحنين محال، وتمر عامة الأوقات ولا توجد الشهادة باللسان بل من الأحوال ما ينهي المرء فيه أن يقول آمنت بالكتب والنبيين والبعث ونحو ذلك كما في الصلوات وكما في حال كونه في الكنيف، وكما في حال خروج البول والغائط منه ومحال ارتفاع فرض الإيمان أو النهي عنه ما دام التكليف باقيًا أو القول بكراهيته حال وجود العبادة التي لا صحة لها إلا به، وكل ذلك يدل على أن الإيمان في الحقيقة هو التصديق، والذي يؤيد هذا كله قوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَنُ بِالْإِيمَن﴾ لم يجعل لهم كفرًا باللسان إذا لم يكن عبارة عن القلب ومنع ذلك أن يكون كفرًا بإيمان القلب فثبت أن القلب هو موضع الإيمان وبه يستدل أن كفر القلب يمنع قول اللسان من أن يكون إيمانًا، والله الموفق.
He verifies that iman is a religion, and religions are believed, and beliefs are in hearts. He verifies that the raising of the act of iman from the tested people is impossible, and most times pass and the testimony by the tongue does not exist, but from the states are those in which a person is prevented from saying 'I believe in the books, the prophets, the resurrection' and like that, as in prayers and as in the state of being in the lavatory, and as in the state of passing urine and stool, and the raising of the obligation of iman or the prohibition of it is impossible as long as the commission remains, or the saying of its dislike in the state of performing an act of worship that has no validity except through it; and all that indicates that iman in reality is tasdiq (affirmation). And what supports all this is His statement, the Exalted: 'Except one who is compelled while his heart is reassured in iman' – He did not make their verbal disbelief (kufr) as disbelief when it was not an expression of the heart, and He prevented that from being disbelief due to the iman of the heart; so it is established that the heart is the locus of iman, and by it it is inferred that the disbelief of the heart prevents the speech of the tongue from being iman. And Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a proof that iman (faith) is essentially tasdiq (affirmation) in the heart, not necessarily verbal confession. The author, Nasafi, begins by stating that iman is a religion (din), and religions are matters of belief, and beliefs reside in the heart. He then provides a multi-step proof: First, it is impossible for the act of iman to be entirely absent from those under obligation (mukallaf), yet there are many times when verbal utterance of the shahada is not performed—such as during prayer (when one cannot speak other words), in the lavatory, or while passing urine or stool. During such states, the obligation of iman cannot be lifted, nor can it be disliked, because the act of worship being performed (prayer) has no validity without iman. Therefore, the constant presence of iman in these situations shows that iman is not dependent on verbal expression. Second, he cites Quran 16:106, which states that one compelled to utter words of disbelief retains his iman if his heart is serene in faith. Allah does not consider the verbal utterance as disbelief because it does not reflect the heart. This proves that the heart is the locus of iman, and that disbelief in the heart prevents verbal confession from being iman. Thus, iman is essentially tasdiq in the heart.

Key Terms
الإيمان (iman)
التصديق (tasdiq)
القلب (heart)
الشهادة باللسان (verbal testimony)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think iman is simply verbal confession.
Correction: This passage shows it is fundamentally inner affirmation.

Checkpoint

B) The agreement of all scholars.
C) The definition of iman in the Quran as 'doing good deeds'.
D) The fact that iman increases with good deeds.

Key Takeaway
Iman is essentially tasdiq (affirmation) in the heart, and verbal confession alone does not constitute faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Iman is Affirmation, Not Mere Knowledge: Refuting Jahm
Nasafi refutes Jahm's view that iman is mere knowledge, arguing tasdiq is essential.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that faith (iman) requires heartfelt affirmation (tasdiq) and not just intellectual knowledge (ma'rifa).

Core Idea
Knowledge without affirmation is not faith—only tasdiq distinguishes believer from denier.

In this passage, Nasafi directly engages with a heretical view that reduces iman to mere intellectual assent. He shows that the very structure of opposites—iman vs. kufr, tasdiq vs. takdhib—demonstrates that knowledge alone cannot constitute faith. Using the example of the Meccan polytheists who knew the Prophet but denied him, he drives home the point that the heart's affirmation is indispensable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice how Nasafi defines iman and its opposite.
The passage includes a header in brackets which is part of the text.
2
Identify key definitions
Find where Nasafi states that iman is tasdiq, kufr is takdhib, and the opposite of knowledge is ignorance/denial, not takdhib.
3
Understand the argument from opposites
Reflect on why the contradiction between tasdiq and takdhib is more fundamental than the contradiction between knowledge and ignorance.
This is the core logical move of the passage.
4
Consider the example of the obstinate Meccans
Think about how the example of the Quraysh knowing the Prophet but rejecting him illustrates the point.
The Quranic reference (6:20) is implicit.
5
Apply the lesson
Ask yourself: What does this say about the nature of faith? Is it merely intellectual or does it require a deeper commitment?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[المعرفة لا تكفي بل لابد من تصديق القلب]: ثم بالقلب يكون التصديق لما مر أن الإيمان يكون بالقلب والإيمان هو التصديق، وليست المعرفة الخالية عن التصديق إيمانًا كما ظن جهم وجماعة أن الإيمان هو المعرفة لما أن الإيمان هو التصديق ثم ضد الإيمان هو الكفر، والكفر هو التكذيب والتكذيب ينافي التصديق لا المعرفة إذ ما يضادها النكرة والجهالة، وليس كل من جهل حقا يكذب به. يحققه أن الإيمان بجميع الأنبياء والرسل وبجميع الكتب وجميع الملائكة ثابت وهو التصديق، والمعرفة بأعيانهم منعدمة، وأهل العناد كانوا يعرفونه كما يعرفون أبناءهم وكانوا يكتمون الحق وهم يعلمون، ولم يثبت لهم الإيمان بتلك المعرفة لانعدام التصديق وثبوت ما يضاده وهو التكذيب، والله الموفق.
[Knowledge is not sufficient; rather, affirmation of the heart is necessary]: Then affirmation (tasdiq) is by the heart, as has passed, that iman is by the heart and iman is tasdiq, and knowledge (ma'rifa) devoid of tasdiq is not iman, as Jahm and a group supposed that iman is knowledge, because iman is tasdiq, and the opposite of iman is kufr, and kufr is takdhib (denial), and takdhib contradicts tasdiq, not knowledge, since what contradicts it is nukra (denial) and jahala (ignorance), and not everyone who is ignorant of a truth denies it. He verifies that iman in all the prophets and messengers and in all the books and all the angels is established, and it is tasdiq, while knowledge of their individuals is absent, and the people of obstinacy knew him (the Prophet) as they knew their own sons, and they concealed the truth while they knew, and iman was not established for them due to that knowledge because of the absence of tasdiq and the presence of its opposite, which is takdhib. And Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that iman (faith) is simply knowledge (ma'rifa). Nasafi first restates that iman is tasdiq (affirmation) in the heart. He then argues that knowledge devoid of tasdiq does not constitute iman, contrary to the opinion of Jahm ibn Safwan and his followers, who claimed iman is merely knowledge. Nasafi's reasoning is that the opposite of iman is kufr (disbelief), and kufr is takdhib (denial). Takdhib directly contradicts tasdiq, not knowledge. The opposite of knowledge is ignorance (jahl) or denial (nukra), not necessarily takdhib. Therefore, knowledge is not the same as iman. To illustrate, he points out that iman requires believing in all prophets, messengers, books, and angels collectively, while detailed knowledge of their individual identities may be absent; yet iman exists with affirmation. Conversely, the obstinate disbelievers of Mecca knew the Prophet Muhammad as they knew their own sons (Quran 6:20), but they concealed the truth and did not have iman. Their knowledge did not benefit them because they lacked affirmation (tasdiq) and instead possessed denial (takdhib). Thus, knowledge alone is insufficient; affirmation of the heart is necessary for iman.

Key Terms
المعرفة (ma'rifa)
التصديق (tasdiq)
التكذيب (takdhib)
جهم (Jahm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that intellectual knowledge of God or the Prophet is sufficient for faith.
Correction: Nasafi shows that knowledge alone is not enough; the heart must actively affirm (tasdiq) what it knows. The disbelievers had knowledge but lacked tasdiq, so they were not believers.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi argue that knowledge (ma'rifa) is insufficient for iman?
A) Because knowledge is only about God, not the prophets.
B) Because the opposite of iman is denial (takdhib), which contradicts affirmation (tasdiq), not knowledge.
C) Because knowledge requires memorization, which many believers lack.
D) Because the disbelievers had no knowledge at all.

Key Takeaway
Iman requires the heart's affirmation (tasdiq); mere knowledge (ma'rifa) without it is insufficient and cannot save a person from disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you have knowledge about God and His Messenger but find your heart not fully submitting? The Quraysh knew the truth yet refused it. Examine your own tasdiq—where is your heart truly leaning?
?
Is there an area of your life where you intellectually acknowledge the truth of Islam but your actions reflect denial? That is a form of takdhib. What practical step will you take today to replace that denial with affirmation?
?
When you recite the Shahada, is it a mere repetition or an active affirmation that rejects every falsehood? Ponder the weight of tasdiq: you are declaring your opposition to takdhib. How will you live that out today?

Iman in Essence Does Not Increase or Decrease
Nasafi defines iman and argues its essence does not change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why iman, being tasdiq (affirmation), is inherently not subject to increase or decrease, and why acts of obedience or sin do not affect its essence.

Core Idea
Iman is a single, indivisible affirmation; it cannot be increased or decreased.

Imam Nasafi begins by establishing the nature of iman as tasdiq. Since it is a single act of the heart, it cannot grow by adding acts of obedience or shrink by sins. This lesson unpacks his logical argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Nasafi defines iman as tasdiq and immediately argues that it is not subject to increase.
The passage uses logical deduction: if something cannot increase, then decrease only by non-existence.
2
Understand the definition of tasdiq
Tasdiq (affirmation) is a single act of the heart. Nasafi asserts that it is not subject to increase because it is a complete act in itself.
This is a key premise: tasdiq is not quantitative.
3
Follow the logical argument
Since tasdiq cannot increase, any increase would require adding another like act, which would be a separate act, not an increase in the original. Similarly, decrease only through non-existence.
Thus, acts of obedience do not add to the essence, nor do sins subtract from it.
4
Apply to actions
Nasafi concludes that iman does not increase by performing acts of obedience nor decrease by committing sins.
This refutes the view that good deeds strengthen iman in its essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص]: وإذا كان الإيمان هو التصديق وهو في نفسه مما لا يتزايد وما لا يتزايد فلا نقصان له إلا بالعدم ولا زيادة عليه إلا بانضمام مثله إليه، فلا زيادة إذا للإيمان بانضمام الطاعات إليه، ولا نقصان بارتكاب المعاصي، إذ التصديق في الحالين على ما كان قبلهما فكان تأويل ما ورد من الزيادة في الإيمان على ما روى عن أبي حنيفة - رحمه الله - أنهم كانوا آمنوا في الجملة ثم يأتي فرض بعد فرض فيؤمن بكل فرض جاء فيزداد إيمانه بالتفسير مع إيمانه بالجملة وإن كان بالجملة في التحقيق إيمان به، وقد روى عن ابن عباس - رضي الله عنهما - هذا التأويل أيضا وكذا الثبات على الإيمان والدوام عليه زيادة عليه في كل ساعة إذ يوجد في كل ساعة مثل ما انعدم في الأولى كما يوجد درهم ثم يزداد عليه في كل ساعة درهم إلا أن تلك الزيادة في نفسه إذ هو غير محتمل للتجزؤ، ويحتمل الزيادة عليه أن يزداد نوره وضياؤه في القلوب بالأعمال الصالحة وينتقص ذلك بالمعاصي إذ الإيمان له ضياء ونور على ما قال تعالى: ﴿ يُرِيدُونَ لِيُطْفِئُوا نُورَ اللَّهِ بِأَفْرَهِهِمْ ﴾ وقال تعالى: ﴿ أَفَمَن شَرَحَ اللهُ صَدْرَهُ لِلإِسْلَامِ فَهُوَ عَلَى نُورٍ مِّن رَّبِّهِ ﴾ فأما هو في ذاته فلا
[Iman does not increase nor decrease]: And when iman is tasdiq (affirmation), and it is in itself not subject to increase, and what is not subject to increase then there is no decrease for it except by non-existence, and no increase upon it except by addition of its like to it; so there is no increase for iman by addition of acts of obedience to it, and no decrease by committing sins, since tasdiq in both states is as it was before them. So the interpretation of what has come concerning the increase in iman is according to what was narrated from Abu Hanifa – may Allah have mercy on him – that they believed in summary (al-jumla), then a particular obligation came after another obligation, so he believed in each obligation that came, so his iman increased in detail (al-tafsir) along with his iman in summary, although in reality the summary already contains iman in it. And this interpretation was also narrated from Ibn Abbas – may Allah be pleased with them both. Likewise, persistence in iman and continuance upon it is an increase upon it every hour, for there exists every hour the like of what ceased in the first, just as a dirham exists and then another dirham is added to it every hour, except that that increase is upon itself (in its essence) because it is not susceptible to division. And it is possible that increase occurs upon it in that its light and radiance in the hearts increase through righteous deeds, and that decreases through sins, for iman has radiance and light according to His saying, the Exalted: 'They want to extinguish the light of Allah with their mouths' and His saying: 'Is he whose breast Allah has expanded for Islam, so he is upon a light from his Lord?' As for it in itself, it does not (increase or decrease).
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument on whether iman (faith) can increase or decrease. The author, Nasafi, begins by asserting that iman is tasdiq (affirmation), and tasdiq in itself is not capable of increase because it is a single indivisible act of the heart. It can only be lost entirely (non-existence) or have another like it added—but that would be a separate act, not an increase of the original. Therefore, performing acts of obedience does not add to the essence of iman, nor do sins subtract from it. To reconcile scriptural verses that speak of increase in iman, Nasafi cites two interpretations: First, from Abu Hanifa, that believers initially have iman in summary (al-jumla), and as new obligations are revealed, they affirm each one in detail (al-tafsir). This is an increase in the object of iman, not in the essence of the act of iman itself. Second, persistence in iman moment by moment can be considered an increase because each moment's affirmation is like a new dirham added to the previous one—but this is a numerical succession, not an increase in the original quality. However, Nasafi clarifies that iman has a light and radiance (nur wa diya') in the heart that can increase or decrease with righteous deeds or sins, as indicated by Quranic verses. But the essence of iman (the tasdiq itself) remains unchanged. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the conclusion is that iman in its essence does not increase or decrease.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
الزيادة
النقصان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Performing more good deeds directly increases the substance of one's iman.
Correction: According to Nasafi, the essence of iman (tasdiq) remains unchanged; increase or decrease applies only to its light or radiance, not to the affirmation itself.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the only way iman can decrease?
A) By committing sins
B) By non-existence
C) By losing knowledge
D) By doubt

Key Takeaway
Iman as tasdiq is a single, indivisible act that cannot be increased or decreased by external actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the essence of your iman does not increase by your good deeds or decrease by your sins, what does that reveal about your reliance on your actions for spiritual security? Does this teaching make you examine whether your tasdiq is truly genuine and present, or do you take it for granted?
?
Nasafi argues that iman is a single act of affirmation. Have you ever experienced a moment when your iman felt stronger or weaker? How does this teaching challenge your personal feelings? Will you now seek to affirm your tasdiq with greater sincerity, knowing it is the only thing that matters in the essence of iman?
?
This passage strips iman down to a bare affirmation. Does that comfort you—knowing that your deeds do not change its core—or does it unsettle you, because it means you cannot rely on your deeds to build it? What will you do with this freedom: use it as a license to sin, or use it to focus entirely on the quality of your tasdiq?

Apparent Increase in Iman: Interpretation and Light
Nasafi explains the interpretations of increase in iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nuanced interpretations of apparent increase in iman, including increase in detail, persistence, and the increase of its light and radiance.

Core Idea
Increase in iman refers to its detail, persistence, or radiance, not its essence.

Having established that the essence of iman does not change, Nasafi addresses scriptural references to increase. He presents interpretations from Abu Hanifa and others, explaining how iman can be said to increase in detail, through persistence, and in its light and radiance, while its core remains unchanged.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the three distinct ways increase is explained: detail (tafsir), persistence (thabat), and light (nur/diya').
The passage also includes Quranic evidence for the light aspect.
2
Understand the detail interpretation
Nasafi reports from Abu Hanifa that believers initially have iman in summary (al-jumla). When new obligations come, they affirm each in detail (al-tafsir), which is an increase in the object of faith, not in the act itself.
This reconciles verses that speak of increasing iman.
3
Understand the persistence interpretation
Persistence in iman moment by moment is like adding a new dirham each hour. This is a numerical succession, not an increase in quality.
It is a manner of speaking, not essential change.
4
Distinguish essence from light
Iman has a light and radiance in the heart that can increase with righteous deeds and decrease with sins, as supported by Quranic verses. But the essence of iman (tasdiq) itself remains unchanged.
This explains why believers feel their faith strengthen without altering its core.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص]: وإذا كان الإيمان هو التصديق وهو في نفسه مما لا يتزايد وما لا يتزايد فلا نقصان له إلا بالعدم ولا زيادة عليه إلا بانضمام مثله إليه، فلا زيادة إذا للإيمان بانضمام الطاعات إليه، ولا نقصان بارتكاب المعاصي، إذ التصديق في الحالين على ما كان قبلهما فكان تأويل ما ورد من الزيادة في الإيمان على ما روى عن أبي حنيفة - رحمه الله - أنهم كانوا آمنوا في الجملة ثم يأتي فرض بعد فرض فيؤمن بكل فرض جاء فيزداد إيمانه بالتفسير مع إيمانه بالجملة وإن كان بالجملة في التحقيق إيمان به، وقد روى عن ابن عباس - رضي الله عنهما - هذا التأويل أيضا وكذا الثبات على الإيمان والدوام عليه زيادة عليه في كل ساعة إذ يوجد في كل ساعة مثل ما انعدم في الأولى كما يوجد درهم ثم يزداد عليه في كل ساعة درهم إلا أن تلك الزيادة في نفسه إذ هو غير محتمل للتجزؤ، ويحتمل الزيادة عليه أن يزداد نوره وضياؤه في القلوب بالأعمال الصالحة وينتقص ذلك بالمعاصي إذ الإيمان له ضياء ونور على ما قال تعالى: ﴿ يُرِيدُونَ لِيُطْفِئُوا نُورَ اللَّهِ بِأَفْرَهِهِمْ ﴾ وقال تعالى: ﴿ أَفَمَن شَرَحَ اللهُ صَدْرَهُ لِلإِسْلَامِ فَهُوَ عَلَى نُورٍ مِّن رَّبِّهِ ﴾ فأما هو في ذاته فلا
[Iman does not increase nor decrease]: And when iman is tasdiq (affirmation), and it is in itself not subject to increase, and what is not subject to increase then there is no decrease for it except by non-existence, and no increase upon it except by addition of its like to it; so there is no increase for iman by addition of acts of obedience to it, and no decrease by committing sins, since tasdiq in both states is as it was before them. So the interpretation of what has come concerning the increase in iman is according to what was narrated from Abu Hanifa – may Allah have mercy on him – that they believed in summary (al-jumla), then a particular obligation came after another obligation, so he believed in each obligation that came, so his iman increased in detail (al-tafsir) along with his iman in summary, although in reality the summary already contains iman in it. And this interpretation was also narrated from Ibn Abbas – may Allah be pleased with them both. Likewise, persistence in iman and continuance upon it is an increase upon it every hour, for there exists every hour the like of what ceased in the first, just as a dirham exists and then another dirham is added to it every hour, except that that increase is upon itself (in its essence) because it is not susceptible to division. And it is possible that increase occurs upon it in that its light and radiance in the hearts increase through righteous deeds, and that decreases through sins, for iman has radiance and light according to His saying, the Exalted: 'They want to extinguish the light of Allah with their mouths' and His saying: 'Is he whose breast Allah has expanded for Islam, so he is upon a light from his Lord?' As for it in itself, it does not (increase or decrease).
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument on whether iman (faith) can increase or decrease. The author, Nasafi, begins by asserting that iman is tasdiq (affirmation), and tasdiq in itself is not capable of increase because it is a single indivisible act of the heart. It can only be lost entirely (non-existence) or have another like it added—but that would be a separate act, not an increase of the original. Therefore, performing acts of obedience does not add to the essence of iman, nor do sins subtract from it. To reconcile scriptural verses that speak of increase in iman, Nasafi cites two interpretations: First, from Abu Hanifa, that believers initially have iman in summary (al-jumla), and as new obligations are revealed, they affirm each one in detail (al-tafsir). This is an increase in the object of iman, not in the essence of the act of iman itself. Second, persistence in iman moment by moment can be considered an increase because each moment's affirmation is like a new dirham added to the previous one—but this is a numerical succession, not an increase in the original quality. However, Nasafi clarifies that iman has a light and radiance (nur wa diya') in the heart that can increase or decrease with righteous deeds or sins, as indicated by Quranic verses. But the essence of iman (the tasdiq itself) remains unchanged. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the conclusion is that iman in its essence does not increase or decrease.

Key Terms
التفسير
الجملة
النور
الضياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'increase' of iman mentioned in the Quran refers to an increase in the essential act of affirmation.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that it refers to increase in detail, persistence, or light/radiance, not in the essence of tasdiq.

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa's interpretation, how does iman increase when a new obligation comes?
A) The essence of tasdiq grows
B) The believer affirms in detail what was already believed in summary
C) The believer receives a new revelation
D) The believer’s doubt decreases

Key Takeaway
Apparent increase in iman is interpreted as increase in detail, persistence, or light, not in the essence of tasdiq.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your iman's essence may be intact, but how much light is in your heart right now? What sin have you committed today that dimmed that light? Will you repent now, this moment, to restore it and increase its radiance through good deeds?
?
You claim to believe in summary, but do you believe in every obligation Allah has sent? Which specific command from Allah are you neglecting right now? How will you act on this lesson's teaching to increase your iman in detail by obeying that command starting today?
?
The lesson says persistence on iman every hour is like adding a new dirham. But are you truly persisting every hour? Identify one hour today when you were forgetful of Allah. What practical step will you take to ensure you renew your iman consciously each hour from now on?

Faith as Assent: No Increase or Decrease
Nasafi defines faith as tasdiq and argues it cannot increase or decrease.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in the Maturidi view, faith is inner assent and does not increase or decrease through actions.

Core Idea
Faith is inner assent—fixed, not fluctuating with deeds.

Imam al-Nasafi here addresses a central question in Islamic theology: does faith increase and decrease? He grounds his answer in the definition of faith itself. Before we can judge its change, we must understand its essence. This passage establishes that faith is simply assent, which is a unitary act unaffected by external actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the first part: faith is affirmation (tasdiq). Notice that this defines faith as an inner act of the heart, not a combination of belief and deeds.
This is crucial for understanding the rest.
2
Follow the logic of increase
The author argues that what does not increase cannot decrease except by vanishing. Do you see why? Ask yourself: can a simple act like assent come in degrees?
3
Apply to actions
Now see the conclusion: obedience and sin do not affect faith. Does this challenge your prior understanding? The commentary explains the reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان الإيمان هو التصديق وهو في نفسه مما لا يتزايد وما لا يتزايد فلا نقصان له إلا بالعدم ولا زيادة عليه إلا بانضمام مثله إليه، فلا زيادة إذا للإيمان بانضمام الطاعات إليه، ولا نقصان بارتكاب المعاصي، إذ التصديق في الحالين على ما كان قبلهما
And when faith is affirmation, and in itself it is not of the kind that increases, and what does not increase has no decrease except by non-existence and no increase except by the addition of its like to it, then there is no increase for faith by the addition of acts of obedience to it, nor decrease by committing sins, for affirmation in both cases is as it was before them.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a definition and a ruling concerning the nature of faith (iman). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, first defines faith as affirmation (tasdiq) of the heart. He then explains that affirmation in itself is not something that admits of increase or decrease because it is a unitary mental act. If something cannot increase, it cannot decrease except by total negation. Therefore, when a person performs acts of obedience or commits sins, his affirmation remains unchanged, so faith does not increase or decrease through external actions.

Key Terms
الإيمان (iman)
التصديق (tasdiq)
الزيادة (increase)
النقصان (decrease)
الطاعات (acts of obedience)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith increases with good deeds and decreases with sins.
Correction: The author argues that faith is inner assent which is unaffected by external actions; only total negation (loss of belief) would decrease it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the only way faith could increase?
A) By attaching another act of assent to it
B) By committing sins
C) By performing many good deeds
D) It cannot increase at all

Key Takeaway
Faith as inner assent is a single, fixed act of the heart that does not change with obedient or sinful actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your sins do not decrease your inner faith (tasdiq), does that give you a false sense of security? How does this teaching actually demand that you examine the sincerity of your affirmation—is it real or just intellectual?
?
The passage says faith is a single fixed assent. Have you ever felt your faith waver? According to this lesson, what part of you is fluctuating—your heart's affirmation or something else? What does that reveal about the difference between your emotional state and your actual belief?
?
This teaching distinguishes between faith and actions. If actions don't add to your faith, what motivation is left for you to obey? Can you honestly say that you worship out of pure affirmation, not seeking to increase faith? How does that challenge your daily practice?
