Abu Hanifa on Increase in Faith as Specification
Author reports Abu Hanifa's interpretation that faith increases by specification (tafsir).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Hanifa's interpretation that increase in faith is a specification of general faith, not an essential change.

Core Idea
Faith increases in detail, not in essence.

This lesson presents Abu Hanifa's nuanced explanation of how faith 'increases' as described in revelation. He distinguishes between summary faith (al-iman bil-jumla) and detailed specification (tafsir), clarifying that increase applies to explicit belief in specific commands, not to the core of faith itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the key terms: 'summary faith' and 'specification'.
The passage is from a classical kalam work.
2
Identify the two types of faith
Abu Hanifa describes two modes: belief in summary (bil-jumla) and belief by specification (bil-tafsir). Understand the difference.
Summary faith includes everything implicitly; specification makes it explicit.
3
Understand why this interpretation resolves the apparent contradiction
Scriptural texts mention increase in faith. Abu Hanifa's explanation shows that the increase is in the number of explicitly believed propositions, not in the essence of faith itself.
This preserves the idea that faith is a single, unchanging core.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider that faith's essence remains constant; what increases is the explicit affirmation of details that were already implicitly affirmed.
This is a key doctrine in Maturidi kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكان تأويل ما ورد من الزيادة في الإيمان على ما روى عن أبي حنيفة - رحمه الله - أنهم كانوا آمنوا في الجملة ثم يأتي فرض بعد فرض فيؤمن بكل فرض جاء فيزداد إيمانه بالتفسير مع إيمانه بالجملة وإن كان بالجملة في التحقيق إيمان به
Thus the interpretation of what has been reported concerning increase in faith is according to what was narrated from Abu Hanifa - may God have mercy on him - that they had believed in summary, then a command after command comes, and he believes in each command that comes, so his faith increases by specification along with his faith in summary, even though in reality the summary includes that faith.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage provides an interpretation (ta'wil) of scriptural texts that mention increase in faith. The author cites Abu Hanifa's explanation: believers initially have a general faith (iman bil-jumla) in all that God has revealed. When a specific command or detail is revealed, they accept it by a new act of belief, which is a specification of the general faith. This specification is called an increase, but it is not an increase in the essence of faith itself; rather, it is the actualization of previously implicit affirmation. In reality, the general faith already includes belief in all details, but the specification brings it to explicit awareness.

Key Terms
الزيادة (increase)
التفسير (specification)
الإيمان بالجملة (summary faith)
أبو حنيفة (Abu Hanifa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith increases in its essential substance or strength.
Correction: Abu Hanifa argues that increase is in explicit specification, not in the essence of faith itself.

Checkpoint
What does Abu Hanifa mean by 'increase in faith'?
A) The inner assent becomes stronger
B) The number of acts of worship increases faith's substance
C) Belief in specific commands becomes explicit while general faith remains
D) Faith multiplies through good deeds

Key Takeaway
Increase in faith is the unfolding of details already implicitly believed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn a new Islamic ruling, do you immediately accept it as binding on you specifically, or do you mentally push it aside? Your faith in the summary is not enough; each command demands your explicit belief. Will you today search for one command you have not yet specified in your heart and act on it?
?
Is your faith a general conviction that remains comfortable and vague, or does it unfold into specific obedience? Think of a command you dislike. Does your faith increase by specifying that command, or do you waver? If you waver, ask yourself: is your faith really belief in the message of the Prophet?
?
Have you ever used the idea of 'faith in summary' to excuse yourself from specific obligations? This lesson teaches that increase happens precisely when you specify your belief to each new command. Where is your faith currently stuck in generality—and what specific command are you avoiding? Make a concrete commitment today to embrace it explicitly.

Increase in the Light of Faith, Not Its Essence
Author distinguishes iman's fixed essence from its variable light.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the increase and decrease of faith refers to its light and radiance, not its essence.

Core Idea
Faith's essence is fixed; its light waxes and wanes with deeds.

This passage from Imam Nasafi's Tabirat al-Adilla clarifies a common confusion: how can faith increase if it is a single assent? The author distinguishes between the essence of iman (which cannot change) and its light (nur) which increases with good deeds and decreases with sins. Understanding this preserves the definition of iman while allowing for growing spiritual brightness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Notice the author's distinction between essence and light.
2
Identify the key distinction
The author says the increase is not in the essence (fi nafsihi) but in its light (nur) and radiance (diya'). Highlight this contrast.
The essence of iman is indivisible; light can vary.
3
Examine the Quranic proofs
The author quotes two verses. Look at how they support the idea that faith has a light that can be affected by deeds.
The first verse speaks of extinguishing light; the second of being upon light.
4
Reflect on the resolution
Consider how this distinction answers the problem of faith increasing: it is the light that increases, not the core assent.
This preserves the definition of iman as one thing while explaining variations in spiritual experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا أن تلك الزيادة في نفسه إذ هو غير محتمل للتجزؤ، ويحتمل الزيادة عليه أن يزداد نوره وضياؤه في القلوب بالأعمال الصالحة وينتقص ذلك بالمعاصي إذ الإيمان له ضياء ونور على ما قال تعالى: ﴿ يُرِيدُونَ لِيُطْفِئُوا نُورَ اللَّهِ بِأَفْوَاهِهِمْ ﴾ وقال تعالى: ﴿ أَفَمَنْ شَرَحَ اللهُ صَدْرَهُ لِلْإِسْلَامِ فَهُوَ عَلَى نُورٍ مِنْ رَبِّهِ ﴾ فأما هو في ذاته فلا يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان على ما بينا
Except that that increase is not in its essence, for it is not susceptible to division, and it is possible for its light and radiance in hearts to increase through righteous deeds and to decrease through sins, for faith has radiance and light according to what He said: 'They want to extinguish the light of God with their mouths' and He said: 'Is he whose breast God has expanded for Islam upon a light from his Lord?' As for it in its essence, it does not admit increase or decrease as we have explained.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage clarifies a subtle distinction: while the essence of faith (iman) as inner assent cannot be divided or increased, faith also has a light or radiance in the heart that can intensify or diminish. The author quotes two Quranic verses: one speaks of disbelievers trying to extinguish the 'light of God' (interpreted as the light of faith), and the other describes believers as being upon a 'light from their Lord.' This light is not the same as the essence of faith; it is an additional quality that waxes and wanes with good deeds and sins, respectively. Thus, the increase and decrease mentioned in texts refer to this light, not to the core affirmation.

النور (light)
الضياء (radiance)
الأعمال الصالحة (righteous deeds)
المعاصي (sins)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith itself can increase or decrease in its essence.
Correction: The essence of iman is a single assent that does not admit increase or decrease; only its light varies.

Checkpoint

A) The essence of faith
B) The number of beliefs
C) The light and radiance of faith
D) The certainty of faith

Key Takeaway
The light of faith can increase and decrease, but the essence of faith remains fixed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Dilemma of Increase for Deed-Inclusive Faith
Nasafi presents a two-part logical dilemma for those who incorporate deeds into faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why those who include deeds in faith cannot logically claim increase in faith.

Core Idea
If all deeds are faith, no one has complete faith, so increase is impossible.

Nasafi begins by targeting the view that incorporates deeds into the definition of faith. He argues that if every act of worship is part of faith, then faith is never fully attained, and increasing what is incomplete is contradictory. Let's examine this foundational dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Nasafi sets up the condition.
2
Understand the premise
Identify that the argument is directed at those who make deeds from faith. What is their definition?
3
See the consequence
If all deeds are faith, then no one has completed faith. Then increase is on something that is still deficient, which is absurd in kalam logic.
4
Reflect on the second argument
There is also the point that if every deed is already from faith, there is nothing beyond the whole to add. This completes the dilemma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان على ما بينا ، ثم أحق الناس أن يمتنع عن القول بالزيادة على الإيمان هم الذين يجعلون الأعمال من الإيمان، وذلك لأنهم إذا جعلوا الأعمال كلها إيمانًا فلا أحد إذا استكمل الإيمان، والزيادة على ما هو لم يكمل بعد وهو في حد النقصان ،محال، ولأنه ما من عبادة توجد إلا وهي من الإيمان ولا شيء وراء الكل ليتصور أن يكون زيادة باتصاله به. :يوضحه أن الزيادة تكون على ذي النهاية فينتهى ثم يزاد عليه، فأما الزيادة على ما لا نهاية له فمحال إلا أن يقول الإيمان في حق الكل في حد النقصان ثم يزداد بكل طاعة ، فمن كانت طاعاته أكثر كان إيمانه أكثر ، فيقال له إذا على زعمك كما الإيمان غير متصور فكان إيمان كل نبي ومرسل ناقصاً ، ثم نقول: إنا بينا أن الإيمان هو التصديق، وما وجد من الأعمال يساويه في اسم الطاعة والعبادة دون اسم الإيمان، فبوجود شيء منها يزداد من حيث المعنى الذي يشاركه في الاسم دون الذي يخالفه، فيكون بزيادة عمل يوجد ازدياد عباداته وطاععاته لا زيادة إيمانه، كما إذا كان في بيت عشرة من الرجال فدخلت امرأة ذلك البيت كان دخولها يوجب زيادة في الأشخاص والآدميين دون الرجال حتى إن من قال ازداد بدخولها الأشخاص كان صادقًا، وإن قال ازداد الرجال كان كاذبًا فكذا هذا، والله الموفق.
Increase and decrease are possible based on what we have explained. Then the people most entitled to refrain from saying increase in faith are those who make deeds part of faith. Because if they make all deeds faith, then no one has completed faith, and increase upon what has not been completed while it is in a state of deficiency is impossible. And because there is no act of worship except that it is from faith, and there is nothing beyond the whole to be conceived as increase by connection to it. He clarifies: increase is upon a finite thing: it ends and then is increased. As for increase upon what has no end, it is impossible, unless one says that faith with respect to the whole is in a state of deficiency and then increases with every obedience, so whoever has more obediences has more faith. Then it is said to him: According to your claim, since faith is not conceivable, then the faith of every prophet and messenger was deficient. Then we say: We have explained that faith is affirmation (tasdiq), and what exists of deeds shares with it in the name of obedience and worship, not in the name of faith. So by the existence of something of them, it increases in terms of the meaning that shares the name, not that which differs. So by the increase of a deed, his acts of worship and obediences increase, not his faith, just as if in a house there are ten men and a woman enters that house, her entry causes an increase in persons and human beings, not in men, such that if one says 'the persons increased by her entry' he is truthful, but if he says 'the men increased' he is lying. So likewise this, and Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a logical argument against the claim that faith (iman) can increase or decrease. Nasafi begins by stating that those who incorporate deeds into faith are the ones who should refrain from claiming increase, because if faith includes all deeds, then no one has completed faith, and increase upon something incomplete is absurd. He then explains that increase only applies to finite things; if faith is infinite (as the sum of all deeds), increase is impossible. He then considers the opponent's counterargument that faith is initially deficient and increases with each deed. He refutes this by pointing out that on this view, every prophet and messenger would have had deficient faith, which is blasphemous. He then reasserts the Maturidi position: faith is tasdiq (affirmation), while deeds share only the name of obedience and worship, not the reality of faith. Therefore, deeds increase one's acts of obedience, not faith itself. He illustrates this with an analogy: a house with ten men; if a woman enters, the number of persons increases but not the number of men. Similarly, deeds increase the category of obedience but not the category of faith. He concludes with 'والله الموفق' (Allah is the Grantor of success).

Key Terms
الإيمان
الزيادة
النقصان
الأعمال
العبادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Deeds can increase faith itself because they are part of its definition.
Correction: Nasafi argues that including deeds in faith leads to logical absurdities, making increase impossible.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's first argument, why is increase impossible for those who make deeds part of faith?
A) Because faith is infinite.
B) Because no one has completed faith, so increase on the incomplete is absurd.
C) Because deeds are not real.
D) Because increase requires decrease.

Key Takeaway
Those who include deeds in faith cannot logically claim increase, because faith would always be incomplete and there is nothing beyond all deeds to add.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you feel your faith has increased? According to this argument, if deeds are part of faith, your faith was already incomplete. How does that sit with your certainty that you are on the right path?
?
You likely believe your faith grows with obedience. But what if you have missed a deed that was actually required for faith to be complete? Are you willing to face that your faith might always be deficient? How does that change your urgency in seeking knowledge and practice?
?
This passage warns against equating deeds with the essence of faith. Examine your own heart: do you sometimes rely on your deeds to feel secure in your faith? What would it mean if that security is logically unstable? Will you shift your trust from your own deeds to God's mercy alone?

The Logical Refutation of Increase by the Analogy of Finite and Infinite
Nasafi uses the finite-infinite distinction to argue against increase and refutes the counterargument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why increase on an infinite thing is impossible and how that refutes the claim of increase in faith.

Core Idea
Increase only applies to finite things; faith defined as sum of deeds is infinite, so increase is impossible.

Nasafi now explains a fundamental logical principle: increase only occurs on something that has an end. If faith is defined as the collection of all deeds (which are limitless), it becomes infinite and cannot accept increase. He then addresses a potential objection and shows its absurd consequence that even prophets would have deficient faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the clarification
Read Nasafi's explanation that increase is on finite things. Understand the logic.
Increase presupposes a termination point.
2
Apply to faith
If faith is the sum of all deeds, it has no limit, so increase is impossible.
3
Consider the objection
The opponent might say faith is initially deficient and increases with each deed. Nasafi refutes that this would make prophets' faith deficient.
This is an a fortiori argument.
4
Absorb the refutation
If every prophet's faith is deficient on that view, that is unacceptable. So the objection fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان على ما بينا ، ثم أحق الناس أن يمتنع عن القول بالزيادة على الإيمان هم الذين يجعلون الأعمال من الإيمان، وذلك لأنهم إذا جعلوا الأعمال كلها إيمانًا فلا أحد إذا استكمل الإيمان، والزيادة على ما هو لم يكمل بعد وهو في حد النقصان ،محال، ولأنه ما من عبادة توجد إلا وهي من الإيمان ولا شيء وراء الكل ليتصور أن يكون زيادة باتصاله به. :يوضحه أن الزيادة تكون على ذي النهاية فينتهى ثم يزاد عليه، فأما الزيادة على ما لا نهاية له فمحال إلا أن يقول الإيمان في حق الكل في حد النقصان ثم يزداد بكل طاعة ، فمن كانت طاعاته أكثر كان إيمانه أكثر ، فيقال له إذا على زعمك كما الإيمان غير متصور فكان إيمان كل نبي ومرسل ناقصاً ، ثم نقول: إنا بينا أن الإيمان هو التصديق، وما وجد من الأعمال يساويه في اسم الطاعة والعبادة دون اسم الإيمان، فبوجود شيء منها يزداد من حيث المعنى الذي يشاركه في الاسم دون الذي يخالفه، فيكون بزيادة عمل يوجد ازدياد عباداته وطاععاته لا زيادة إيمانه، كما إذا كان في بيت عشرة من الرجال فدخلت امرأة ذلك البيت كان دخولها يوجب زيادة في الأشخاص والآدميين دون الرجال حتى إن من قال ازداد بدخولها الأشخاص كان صادقًا، وإن قال ازداد الرجال كان كاذبًا فكذا هذا، والله الموفق.
Increase and decrease are possible based on what we have explained. Then the people most entitled to refrain from saying increase in faith are those who make deeds part of faith. Because if they make all deeds faith, then no one has completed faith, and increase upon what has not been completed while it is in a state of deficiency is impossible. And because there is no act of worship except that it is from faith, and there is nothing beyond the whole to be conceived as increase by connection to it. He clarifies: increase is upon a finite thing: it ends and then is increased. As for increase upon what has no end, it is impossible, unless one says that faith with respect to the whole is in a state of deficiency and then increases with every obedience, so whoever has more obediences has more faith. Then it is said to him: According to your claim, since faith is not conceivable, then the faith of every prophet and messenger was deficient. Then we say: We have explained that faith is affirmation (tasdiq), and what exists of deeds shares with it in the name of obedience and worship, not in the name of faith. So by the existence of something of them, it increases in terms of the meaning that shares the name, not that which differs. So by the increase of a deed, his acts of worship and obediences increase, not his faith, just as if in a house there are ten men and a woman enters that house, her entry causes an increase in persons and human beings, not in men, such that if one says 'the persons increased by her entry' he is truthful, but if he says 'the men increased' he is lying. So likewise this, and Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a logical argument against the claim that faith (iman) can increase or decrease. Nasafi begins by stating that those who incorporate deeds into faith are the ones who should refrain from claiming increase, because if faith includes all deeds, then no one has completed faith, and increase upon something incomplete is absurd. He then explains that increase only applies to finite things; if faith is infinite (as the sum of all deeds), increase is impossible. He then considers the opponent's counterargument that faith is initially deficient and increases with each deed. He refutes this by pointing out that on this view, every prophet and messenger would have had deficient faith, which is blasphemous. He then reasserts the Maturidi position: faith is tasdiq (affirmation), while deeds share only the name of obedience and worship, not the reality of faith. Therefore, deeds increase one's acts of obedience, not faith itself. He illustrates this with an analogy: a house with ten men; if a woman enters, the number of persons increases but not the number of men. Similarly, deeds increase the category of obedience but not the category of faith. He concludes with 'والله الموفق' (Allah is the Grantor of success).

Key Terms
الزيادة
النقصان
الإيمان
طاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith can increase through deeds because deeds are finite and add to faith.
Correction: Nasafi shows that either faith is infinite (if it includes all deeds) and cannot increase, or if it is deficient, then all prophets would have deficient faith—both are impossible.

Checkpoint
What is the absurd consequence Nasafi derives from the opponent's claim that faith is initially deficient and increases with deeds?
A) That faith would become infinite.
B) That prophets would have had deficient faith.
C) That deeds are not really from faith.
D) That increase would be infinite.

Key Takeaway
Increase only applies to finite things; faith defined as all deeds is infinite, and claiming it is deficient leads to the absurdity of deficient prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If faith cannot increase in its essence, what is truly changing when you feel your faith grows stronger? Are you willing to examine your motivation for obedience: do you seek a real increase in faith, or something else?
?
The argument shows that claiming prophets had deficient faith is absurd. Yet, do you ever think of your own faith as 'less than' others? How does this lesson challenge you to stop comparing and instead focus on the reality of iman that is complete from the start?
?
If your faith is infinite, then every act of disobedience cannot diminish it, and every act of obedience cannot increase it. How does that truth affect the urgency of your next sin? Will you still avoid it out of love, or will you excuse it?

Nasafi's Positive Position: Faith as Tasdiq and the Analogy of Men and Women
Nasafi defines faith as tasdiq and uses an analogy to show deeds increase obedience only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's own definition of faith as tasdiq and how the house analogy clarifies that deeds increase obedience, not faith.

Core Idea
Faith is tasdiq; deeds share the name but not the reality, so they increase obedience, not faith.

Having refuted the opponents' claims, Nasafi now presents the Maturidi position: faith is affirmation (tasdiq) by the heart. Deeds are called obedience and worship but are not of the same essence as faith. He illustrates with a simple analogy: a woman entering a house adds to the count of persons but not men. Similarly, deeds add to acts of worship but not to faith itself.

Guided Path
1
Read Nasafi's own statement
Read how Nasafi defines faith as tasdiq and distinguishes deeds.
2
Understand the distinction
Deeds share in the name 'obedience' but not in the name 'faith'. So increase in deeds increases obedience, not faith.
3
Study the analogy
Ten men in a house, a woman enters: persons increase, men do not. This illustrates the distinction.
Apply: deeds are like the woman, faith is like 'men'.
4
Internalize the conclusion
Thus, when a believer performs a good deed, his acts of worship increase, but his faith (tasdiq) remains unchanged.

Refuting the Perfection Verse as Proof of Deficiency
Nasafi refutes the perfection verse as proof of deficiency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi rejects the claim that Qur'an 5:3 implies religion was deficient before its revelation, and see the absurd consequences of that view.

Core Idea
Perfection of religion proves its completeness from the start, not previous deficiency.

Some argue that the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion for you' shows that faith or religion was incomplete before that day. Nasafi finds this claim deeply problematic because it would accuse the Prophet and the early companions of following an imperfect religion. This lesson unpacks his logical refutation and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opponents' claim
Read the passage to see how opponents use the perfection verse to argue that faith can increase, implying past deficiency.
Note that they think the verse proves the religion was incomplete before.
2
Follow Nasafi's counterexample
Nasafi asks: if the religion was incomplete before that verse, then what about the Muhajirun, Ansar, and even the Prophet? They would have been following an incomplete religion, which is absurd.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Connect to faith's nature
Recall that faith is affirmation (tasdiq), which does not increase or decrease; if it changes, it becomes disbelief. This supports the conclusion that perfection verse does not imply previous deficiency.
Faith's immutability is key.
4
Recognize the self-aggrandizement
Nasafi observes that those who claim later completeness are effectively praising themselves above the early Muslims, which is unacceptable.
This is an ad hominem but valid theological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم العجب منهم أنهم يزعمون أن كافرًا لو أسلم وصدق بجميع ما يجب تصديقه صار مؤمنا ثم لو ارتكب من ساعته إثمًا انتقل إيمانه وليس معه إلا التصديق والتصديق لا تزايد له ولو اختل لتبدل بالتكذيب وبطل، ولو لم يختل بقى كاملاً فكان القول ببقائه وثبوت النقص فيه باطلاً، وتعلقهم بقوله تعالى: {الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ} أنه دليل أن الدين كان إلى ذلك اليوم ناقصا. باطل، لأن ذلك يوجب على قولهم أن من مات قبل ذلك من المهاجرين والأنصار الذين شهدوا بدر ا بايوا رسول الله عليه السلام البيعتين جميعًا وبذلوا أنفسهم الله تعالى بمكة مع عظيم ما حل بهم من نكاية العدو وأنواع البلايا كلهم ماتوا على دين ناقص، وكذلك كان رسول الله عليه السلام يدعوهم إلى دين ناقص، وكان يوالي ويعادي عليه، وصاحب هذا القول على دين كامل فإذا سعى في مدح نفسه وتزكيتها وتقديمها على من يعلم أنه بجميع سعيه لا يبلغ مقامًا واحدًا من

Commentary
This passage refutes a further proof used by the opponents. Nasafi first notes the absurdity of the opponents' claim that a convert who sins loses his faith, because faith is only affirmation which does not increase or decrease; if it were to become defective, it would become disbelief. Then he addresses their proof from the Quranic verse 'Today I have perfected your religion for you' (5:3), which they argue shows the religion was incomplete before. Nasafi points out the devastating implication: if the religion was incomplete before that verse, then all the early Muslims, including the Prophet himself, would have been practicing an incomplete religion, which is absurd. He emphasizes that the early companions and the Prophet called to a complete religion, and to claim otherwise is self-aggrandizement. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is clear.

Correction: Nasafi shows this would imply the Prophet and early Muslims followed an incomplete religion, which is absurd. The verse indicates completeness from the start, not a change from deficiency to perfection.

Key Takeaway
The perfection verse does not imply previous deficiency; rather, it affirms that the religion was always complete, and claiming otherwise disrespects the early Muslims and the Prophet.

Nasafi's Refutation of Faith Decrease and the Verse Misinterpretation
Nasafi refutes the claim that faith can decrease and the misinterpretation of the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that faith (affirmation) does not decrease and that the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' does not imply that earlier religion was incomplete.

Core Idea
Faith is immutable affirmation; any defect would turn it into denial.

In this passage, Nasafi tackles two intertwined claims. First, he exposes the logical contradiction in asserting that faith can both remain and be deficient. Then, he shows the absurd consequences of interpreting the perfection verse as implying prior incompleteness. Let's follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opponents' argument
The opponents claim that a convert's faith can be lost by sin, leaving only affirmation (tasdiq), which they say does not increase. They conclude that if faith were defective it would become denial, so it cannot be both remaining and deficient.
Notice the opponents use tasdiq's immutability to argue against deficiency.
2
See Nasafi's refutation of faith decrease
Nasafi points out the inherent contradiction: if tasdiq does not admit increase, it cannot admit deficiency either. To claim faith both remains and is deficient is logically false.
Nasafi's refutation is based on the nature of tasdiq itself.
3
Examine the verse misinterpretation
The opponents use the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' to claim earlier religion was incomplete. Nasafi shows the absurd consequence: if true, all early Muslims who died before that day would have died with incomplete religion, and the Prophet would have preached an incomplete religion.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical force
Nasafi criticizes the opponent for exalting himself above the early Muslims while accusing the Quran of bringing incomplete religion, showing the claim is self-defeating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم العجب منهم أنهم يزعمون أن كافرًا لو أسلم وصدق بجميع ما يجب تصديقه صار مؤمنا ثم لو ارتكب من ساعته إثمًا انتقل إيمانه وليس معه إلا التصديق والتصديق لا تزايد له ولو اختل لتبدل بالتكذيب وبطل، ولو لم يختل بقى كاملاً فكان القول ببقائه وثبوت النقص فيه باطلاً، وتعلقهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ﴾ أنه دليل أن الدين كان إلى ذلك اليوم ناقصا. باطل، لأن ذلك يوجب على قولهم أن من مات قبل ذلك من المهاجرين والأنصار الذين شهدوا بدرا وبايعوا رسول الله عليه السلام البيعتين جميعًا وبذلوا أنفسهم الله تعالى بمكة مع عظيم ما حل بهم من نكاية العدو وأنواع البلايا كلهم ماتوا على دين ناقص، وكذلك كان رسول الله عليه السلام يدعوهم إلى دين ناقص، وكان يوالي ويعادي عليه، وصاحب هذا القول على دين كامل فإذا سعى في مدح نفسه وتزكيتها وتقديمها على من يعلم أنه بجميع سعيه لا يبلغ مقامًا واحدًا من مقاماتهم، ثم هو شهد على كتاب الله تعالى أنه جاء بالدين الناقص إلى ذلك اليوم، وهذا كله باطل.
Then it is surprising from them that they claim that if a disbeliever embraces Islam and affirms all that must be affirmed, he becomes a believer. Then if he commits a sin immediately afterward, his faith transfers [to sin] and he has nothing but affirmation (tasdiq), and affirmation does not admit increase. If it were to become defective, it would change into denial and become void. If it does not become defective, it remains complete. So the statement that it remains and that deficiency is proven in it is false. And their clinging to His statement, the Most High: 'Today I have perfected for you your religion' as evidence that the religion was deficient until that day is false. Because that would entail according to their statement that those who died before that from the Emigrants (Muhajirun) and Helpers (Ansar) who witnessed [the battle of] Badr and gave the two oaths of allegiance to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, and sacrificed themselves for God, the Most High, in Mecca with the great afflictions that befell them from the harm of the enemy and various trials, all of them died upon an incomplete religion. And likewise, the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, used to call them to an incomplete religion and used to ally and oppose based upon it. And the proponent of this statement is upon a complete religion. So he seeks to praise and purify himself and give precedence to himself over those whom he knows that with all his effort he cannot reach one station of their stations. Then he bears witness against the Book of God, the Most High, that it brought an incomplete religion until that day. All of this is false.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that faith does not increase or decrease, and specifically that the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' proves that the religion was incomplete before that day. Nasafi begins by presenting the opponents' argument: they claim that a disbeliever who embraces Islam and affirms all that is required becomes a believer; then if he immediately commits a sin, his faith transfers to sin, leaving him with only affirmation (tasdiq). They assert that affirmation does not admit increase—if it could become defective, it would turn into denial, and if it remains intact, it is complete. Therefore, they argue, saying that faith remains while also admitting deficiency in it is contradictory. Then they cling to the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' as proof that the religion was deficient before that day. Nasafi rejects this outright, calling it false. He shows the absurd consequence: if the verse meant that the religion was incomplete before that moment, then all the great early Muslims—the Muhajirun and Ansar who fought at Badr, gave the two oaths of allegiance, and endured immense hardships in Mecca—died upon an incomplete religion. Moreover, the Prophet himself would have been calling them to an incomplete religion and basing his alliances and enmities on it. Nasafi further points out that the proponent of this view claims to be on a complete religion, thereby exalting himself above those great figures whom he cannot match in station, while simultaneously accusing the Quran of having brought an incomplete religion until that day. All of this, he concludes, is false.

Key Terms
إيمان
تصديق
نقص
كمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith can increase or decrease like a quantity, and the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' proves that earlier religion was incomplete.
Correction: Faith is affirmation (tasdiq), which is immutable; it does not admit increase or decrease. The perfection of religion refers to the completion of legislation, not to removal of deficiency.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why is the claim that the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' proves that earlier religion was incomplete invalid?
A) Because the verse refers only to the perfection of rituals.
B) Because it would imply that the early Muslims died with incomplete religion.
C) Because the verse was revealed after the conquest of Mecca.
D) Because the verse is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
Faith is a single, immutable affirmation; the perfection of religion refers to completion of legislation, not to removal of deficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to have iman, but do you sometimes feel your faith 'decreases' when you sin? According to this lesson, faith is either complete affirmation or denial. Are you complacent in your current state, or do you need to re-examine if your affirmation is truly complete? What step will you take today to ensure your tasdiq is not compromised?
?
When you hear the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion,' do you subtly think your understanding of Islam is more complete than that of the early Muslims? The lesson shows that such thinking is false and arrogant. In what ways do you exalt yourself over the Sahaba, and how can you humble yourself before their station?
?
If faith cannot decrease, then your repentance does not 'increase' faith but reaffirms your original affirmation. Are there any commands of Allah that you are not fully affirming in your life? What is one area where you have been holding back, and how will you fully submit starting now?

Faith as a Real Attribute: The Case of Tasdiq
Defines faith as affirmation (tasdiq) and compares it to real physical attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi definition of faith as affirmation (tasdiq) and how it is considered a real, determinate attribute of the soul, analogous to physical qualities like sitting or blackness.

Core Idea
Faith is a real attribute of the self, not merely a mental state.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi establishes the essential nature of faith (iman). He defines it as heartfelt affirmation (tasdiq) of the Prophet Muhammad's message, and argues that this affirmation is a real, objective attribute that inheres in the soul, just as sitting or blackness are real attributes of bodies. This sets the foundation for understanding why faith is a genuine spiritual reality that transforms the believer, not just a label or a mental construct.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage once, then read the literal English translation. Pay attention to how the author defines faith and what analogy he uses.
The passage begins a new topic: 'Issue of the consequence'.
2
Identify the core definition
Find the phrase that defines faith as 'tasdiq' (affirmation). Notice that it specifies affirmation of the Prophet Muhammad's message from Allah.
3
Understand the analogy
The author says faith makes the self a believer 'like sitting, standing, blackness, whiteness'. Compare these physical attributes: they are real and make the subject what it is. Faith similarly makes the self a believer.
This analogy is key to understanding faith as a real attribute (ma'na).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[مسألة العاقبة]
ثم الإيمان لما كان اسمًا للتصديق وهو على التلخيص تصديق محمد بما جاء به من عند الله تعالى وهو شيء حقيقي معلوم الحد، فإذا حصل بهذا الحد كان الذات به مؤمنا كالقعود والجلوس والسواد والبياض وغير ذلك لما كانت معاني
[Issue of the consequence]
Then, since faith is a name for affirmation (tasdiq), and it is, according to the summary, the affirmation of Muhammad regarding what he brought from Allah Almighty, and it is a real thing of known definition. So when it occurs according to this definition, the self becomes a believer by it, like sitting, standing, blackness, whiteness, and other such meanings.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage introduces a new topic: the nature of faith (iman). It states that faith is a name for tasdiq (affirmation/heartfelt confirmation). In summary, it is the affirmation of Muhammad's truthfulness in all that he brought from Allah. This tasdiq is described as a real (haqiqi) thing with a known definition (hadd). When this definition is realized in a person, that person becomes a believer (mu'min) in the same way that a person becomes 'sitting' through the attribute of sitting, 'standing' through standing, 'black' through blackness, etc. The author compares faith to other real attributes (ma'ani) that inhere in the subject. This suggests that faith is an actual, determinate attribute of the self, not merely a mental state or metaphor. The argument is that just as physical attributes like sitting or color are real and have defined limits (they occur at a specific moment and make the subject described by them), so too faith is a real attribute that makes the person a believer when it occurs.

Key Terms

التصديق
شيء حقيقي
الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith is merely a mental state or linguistic assertion without real existence in the soul.
Correction: The passage argues that faith is a real attribute (ma'na) that inheres in the self, like sitting or blackness, and it makes the self a believer when it occurs. It is not a mere label or external act.

Checkpoint
How does the author characterize faith (iman) in this passage?
A) As a metaphor for good deeds.
B) As a real attribute (ma'na) like sitting or blackness.
C) As a term of approval by the community.
D) As a purely linguistic confession.

Key Takeaway
Faith is a real, determinate attribute of the soul, defined as heartfelt affirmation of the Prophet's message, and it transforms the self into a believer just as physical attributes define a body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Is your faith as constant and identity-shaping as your physical characteristics, or does it fluctuate with moods and circumstances? What would it take for your faith to become a permanent attribute of your self?
?
If faith transforms the self into a believer just as standing makes you a stander, does your life reflect that transformation? In what specific situation this week will you act as if your faith is a real, undeniable attribute rather than an abstract belief?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
Faith is Real and Present, Not Dependent on Future
Nasafi defines faith and refutes the final-end-only view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith is a real, present attribute and why God's foreknowledge of someone's final state does not negate their current reality of faith or disbelief.

Core Idea
God knows the future, but that doesn't make the present unreal.

Imam al-Nasafi begins by defining faith as affirmation of the Prophet. He then presents the controversial view that only the final destiny matters, not the present state. This lesson unpacks his refutation using everyday examples: a living person is called alive, not dead, despite God knowing their death. If we judged by the future alone, we would have to say everyone is already in the Hereafter — an absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Let the argument unfold as Nasafi wrote it.
Pay attention to his clear analogy.
2
Identify the definition of faith
Notice that Nasafi defines faith as affirmation (taṣdīq). It is a real attribute with a known limit, like sitting or blackness.
This definition grounds the entire refutation.
3
Understand the opposing view
The Ash'arites and Kharijites claim that only the final end (ʿāqiba) matters. Under that view, a person could be called a believer now even while worshipping idols, if God knows they will die a believer.
This is the view Nasafi rejects.
4
Analyze the analogy of present attributes
Nasafi argues that God knows a living person as living, not as dead, even though He knows they will die. Similarly, a sitting person is sitting, not standing, despite future changes. Realities in the present are determined by current states, not future ones.
This analogy is the core of the refutation.
5
Reflect on the absurd consequence
If the future determined present labels, we would have to say everyone is now in the Hereafter and every dead person is alive. That is clearly false, so the opposing doctrine is false.
This conclusion seals the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الإيمان لما كان اسمًا للتصديق وهو على التلخيص تصديق محمد بما جاء به من عند الله تعالى وهو شيء حقيقي معلوم الحد، فإذا حصل بهذا الحد كان الذات به مؤمنا كالقعود والجلوس والسواد والبياض وغير ذلك لما كانت معاني معلومة الحد متى وجدت بحقيقتها كان الذات بها قاعدًا جالسًا أسود أبيض فكذا هذا، ثم إذا كان كذلك لا معنى لقول الأشعرية ومن تقدمهم من الخوارج كنجدة الحروري وطوائف من الناس أن لا عبرة لإيمان من وجد منه التصديق للحال ولا لكفر من وجد منه التكذيب بل العبرة للعاقبة، فإن كان في علم الله تعالى أن هذا الشخص المعين يختم له بالإيمان فهو للحال مؤمن وإن كان مكذبا لله تعالى ولرسوله عليه السلام ساجدًا للصنم، وإن كان في علمه أنه يختم له بالكفر – نعوذ بالله - يكون في الحال كافرًا وإن كان مصدقًا لله تعالى ولرسوله فهذا لا معنى له، لأن الحقائق لم تعرف معدومة باعتبار العلم أنها تنعدم فإن الله يعلم الحي حيا ولا يعلمه للحال ميتا وإن كان يعلم أنه يموت لا محالة، وكذا هذا من الجالس والقائم والأسود والأبيض وكل وصف وحال للآدمي، ولو كان الأمر على ما تزعمون لكان ينبغي أن نكون نحن الآن في الآخرة وأن كل ميت كان حيًا لأن عاقبة الأمر هكذا، وحيث كان هذا باطلاً خارجاً عن المعارف دل على بطلان ذلك المذهب، والله الموفق. فإن قالوا: أليس إذا علم الله تعالى أنه يختم له بالإيمان فهو ولي الله، وإذا علم أنه يختم له بالكفر فهو عدو الله تعالى؟ قلنا : الولاية والعداوة تكونان بالإيمان والكفر فمن كفر بعد إيمانه كان وليًا فصار عدواً وكذا القلب، والتغير على الولي والعدو دون الولاية والعداوة كما في العلم والمعلوم والإخبار والمخبر عنه، والله الموفق.
Then, since faith (al-īmān) is a name for affirmation (al-taṣdīq), and it is, in summary, affirmation of Muhammad with what he brought from God Almighty, and it is a real thing whose limit is known, so when it occurs according to this limit, the essence becomes by it a believer (mu'min), like sitting and standing and blackness and whiteness and other such things, since they are meanings whose limits are known; whenever they occur in their reality, the essence becomes by it sitting, standing, black, white — similarly this. Then, if that is so, there is no meaning to the statement of the Ash'arites and those before them from the Kharijites like Najda al-Ḥarūrī and groups of people, that there is no consideration for the faith of one in whom affirmation is found presently, nor for the disbelief of one in whom denial is found; rather consideration is for the final end (al-ʿāqiba). So if it is in the knowledge of God Almighty that this specific person will be sealed with faith, then he is presently a believer even if he is denying God Almighty and His Messenger, prostrating to an idol; and if it is in His knowledge that he will be sealed with disbelief — we seek refuge in God — he is presently a disbeliever even if he is affirming God Almighty and His Messenger. This has no meaning, because realities are not known as non-existent by virtue of knowledge that they will cease; for God knows the living as living and does not know him presently as dead, even though He knows that he will die without fail. And likewise this applies to the sitter and the stander, the black and the white, and every description and state of a human. If the matter were as you claim, it would be necessary that we are now in the Hereafter and that every dead person was alive, because the final end is like that. And since this is false and outside of known things, it indicates the falsity of that doctrine. And God is the Grantor of success. If they say: Does not God Almighty, when He knows that he will be sealed with faith, make him a friend (walī) of God, and when He knows that he will be sealed with disbelief, make him an enemy (ʿaduww) of God? We say: Friendship and enmity come about through faith and disbelief; so whoever disbelieves after his faith was a friend, then becomes an enemy, and similarly the opposite. Change occurs upon the friend and the enemy, not upon friendship and enmity, just as in knowledge and the known, and in informing and the thing informed about. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the doctrine that considers only the final end (al-ʿāqiba) for determining a person's faith or disbelief, ignoring their present state. Imam al-Nasafi begins by establishing the definition of faith (īmān) as affirmation (taṣdīq) of Muhammad with what he brought from God. He argues that faith is a real attribute with a known limit: when it exists, the person is truly a believer, just as sitting or blackness are real attributes. Then he attacks the view of the Ash'arites and earlier Kharijites (like Najda al-Ḥarūrī) who claim that the only consideration is the final end. Under that view, a person who currently affirms but is destined for disbelief would be considered a disbeliever now, and one who denies but is destined for faith would be considered a believer now. Al-Nasafi calls this meaningless because realities are not negated by future knowledge. He gives the analogy: God knows a living person as living, not as dead, even though He knows he will die. Similarly, a sitting person is sitting, not standing, even if God knows he will stand later. If the future determined the present, we would have to consider everyone in the Hereafter now. Since that is absurd, the doctrine is false. Then he answers a potential objection: Does God's knowledge of the final outcome make the person a friend or enemy now? He responds that friendship (wilāya) and enmity (ʿadāwa) are contingent on faith and disbelief; they change when the person changes. The change applies to the person (the friend or enemy), not to the abstract concepts of friendship and enmity, just as knowledge and the known change accordingly. Thus the refutation is complete.

Key Terms
إيمان
تصديق
عاقبة
أشعرية
خوارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's foreknowledge of a person's final state makes their present faith or disbelief irrelevant.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that present realities are determined by current states, not future outcomes. God knows the present as it is.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, why is it false to say a person is a believer because God knows they will die a believer, even if they are currently denying God?
A) Because God's knowledge is not relevant to human labels.
B) Because realities are known by their present state, not by future knowledge.
C) Because faith is not a real attribute.
D) Because the final end is unknowable.

Key Takeaway
Faith is a real present attribute; God's knowledge of the future does not change current reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your faith were judged solely by your present affirmation of the Prophet, without any hope of future salvation, would you be confident right now that you are a true believer? What would need to change in your daily habits to make your current faith more real?
?
Nasafi compares faith to sitting or standing—properties that are true at the moment. Is your faith that tangible and concrete in your life? Or do you sometimes rely on a vague 'insha'Allah I'll be good in the end' while ignoring your present state of heedlessness?
?
What does it mean for you personally that God knows the living as living and not as dead? How should that affect the way you view your own spiritual state today, instead of postponing repentance to an uncertain future?

The Objection About Divine Friendship and Enmity Answered
Nasafi answers the objection about divine friendship and enmity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi answers the objection that God's foreknowledge determines friendship or enmity in this life, by distinguishing between the person and the abstract relationship.

Core Idea
Friendship and enmity change with the person's state, not with God's foreknowledge.

Having refuted the view that only the final end matters, al-Nasafi addresses a potential objection: doesn't God's knowledge of the final outcome make someone a friend or enemy even now? His response is subtle — friendship and enmity are contingent on current faith or disbelief, and they change when the person changes. The change applies to the person, not the abstract concepts.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The opponent asks: if God knows someone will be sealed with faith, does that not make them a friend (walī) of God now? Similarly for enmity.
This objection seems to challenge the previous refutation.
2
Understand al-Nasafi's response
He answers that friendship and enmity are based on faith and disbelief. They change when the person changes: a believer who becomes a disbeliever changes from friend to enemy.
3
Grasp the distinction
Change occurs on the person (the friend or enemy), not on the abstract relationships of friendship and enmity. This is analogous to knowledge and the known — when the known changes, knowledge changes accordingly.
This preserves the present reality of faith/disbelief.

The passage says change happens on the person, not on friendship and enmity. If you were to die tonight, would you be in a state of friendship or enmity? What change must you make now to secure friendship?
?
Think of a moment when you chose disbelief over faith, even briefly. Did you realize that in that moment you became an enemy? How does that reality affect your resolve to repent and return to friendship?

The Fallacy of Judging Faith by Final Outcome
Nasafi refutes the Muwafat theory by establishing that present attributes are determined by present existence, not future knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that present faith or disbelief should be judged by present reality, not by divine foreknowledge of the final outcome.

Core Idea
Present reality, not future knowledge, determines current faith or disbelief.

In this passage, Nasafi refutes the Muwafat theory which claims that a person's faith or disbelief in this life is determined by their final outcome (al-ʿāqiba) as known by Allah. He begins by establishing a rational principle: when an attribute truly exists in a person, they are described by it. Then he demonstrates the absurd consequences of judging by future knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the principle
Nasafi starts by stating a general principle: when an attribute exists in its reality, the entity is qualified by it. For example, if someone is sitting, they are truly sitting. Read this carefully.
This sets the foundation for his argument.
2
Understand the opposing view
He then quotes the Ash'ari and Khawarij view that present faith has no weight; only the final outcome matters. Note how he summarizes their position.
They argue that if Allah knows someone will die a believer, they are a believer now, even if they are currently denying.
3
Follow the reductio argument
Nasafi exposes the fallacy by analogy: If we judged by future knowledge, we would call a living person dead, a standing person sitting, etc. This leads to the absurd conclusion that we are now in the Hereafter. Consider why this is impossible.
This reductio shows the view is unsound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معلومة الحد متى وجدت بحقيقتها كان الذات بها قاعدًا جالسًا أسود أبيض فكذا هذا، ثم إذا كان كذلك لا معنى لقول الأشعرية ومن تقدمهم من الخوارج كنجدة الحروري وطوائف من الناس أن لا عبرة لإيمان من وجد منه التصديق للحال ولا لكفر من وجد منه التكذيب بل العبرة للعاقبة، فإن كان في علم الله تعالى أن هذا الشخص المعين يختم له بالإيمان فهو للحال مؤمن وإن كان مكذبا لله تعالى ولرسوله عليه السلام ساجدًا للصنم، وإن كان في علمه أنه يختم له بالكفر – نعوذ بالله - يكون في الحال كافرًا وإن كان مصدقًا لله تعالى ولرسوله فهذا لا معنى له، لأن الحقائق لم تعرف معدومة باعتبار العلم أنها تنعدم فإن الله يعلم الحي حيا ولا يعلمه للحال ميتا وإن كان يعلم أنه يموت لا محالة، وكذا هذا من الجالس والقائم والأسود والأبيض وكل وصف وحال للآدمي، ولو كان الأمر على ما تزعمون لكان ينبغي أن نكون نحن الآن في الآخرة وأن كل ميت كان حيًا لأن عاقبة الأمر هكذا، وحيث كان هذا باطلاً خارجاً عن المعارف دل على بطلان ذلك المذهب، والله الموفق. فإن قالوا: أليس إذا علم الله تعالى أنه يختم له بالإيمان فهو ولي الله، وإذا علم أنه يختم له بالكفر فهو عدو الله تعالى؟ قلنا : الولاية والعداوة تكونان بالإيمان والكفر فمن كفر بعد إيمانه كان وليًا فصار عدواً وكذا القلب، والتغير على الولي والعدو دون الولاية والعداوة كما في العلم والمعلوم والإخبار والمخبر عنه، والله الموفق.
The [rationally] known attribute: whenever it exists in its reality, the entity is by it sitting, standing, black, white — so also this. Then, if this is the case, there is no meaning to the statement of the Ash'aris and those before them from the Khawarij like Najda al-Haruri and groups of people: that there is no regard for the faith of one from whom affirmation (tasdiq) is found at present, nor for the disbelief of one from whom denial is found; rather, regard is for the final outcome (al-ʿāqiba). For if it is in the knowledge of Allah Most High that this particular person will be sealed with faith, then he is at present a believer, even if he denies Allah and His Messenger and prostrates to an idol. And if it is in His knowledge that he will be sealed with disbelief — we seek refuge in Allah — he is at present a disbeliever, even if he affirms Allah and His Messenger. This has no meaning, because realities are not known as non-existent by virtue of knowledge that they will become non-existent. For Allah knows the living as living, and He does not know him at present as dead, even though He knows that he will inevitably die. Likewise this applies to the sitting, standing, black, white, and every attribute and state of a human. If the matter were as you claim, then it would be necessary that we now be in the Hereafter, and that every dead person was alive, because the final outcome of the matter is thus. And when this is false and outside of [sound] knowledge, it indicates the falsity of that doctrine. And Allah grants success. If they say: 'Does not Allah, when He knows that he will be sealed with faith, then he is a friend (walī) of Allah; and when He knows that he will be sealed with disbelief, then he is an enemy (ʿaduww) of Allah?' We say: Friendship and enmity occur through faith and disbelief. So whoever disbelieves after his faith was a friend and then becomes an enemy; likewise the opposite. Change occurs upon the friend and enemy, not upon friendship and enmity itself — just as in knowledge and the known, and informing and the informed-about. And Allah grants success.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view (attributed to some Ash'aris and Khawarij) that a person's faith or disbelief in the present is determined by their final state (al-ʿāqiba) as known by Allah. Nasafi begins by establishing a principle: when an attribute (like sitting, standing, black, white) actually exists in its reality, the entity is described by it. Similarly, if affirmation (tasdiq) exists in a person, that person is a believer in reality, regardless of future outcomes. He then states that the contrary view—that present faith has no value and only the final outcome matters—is meaningless. He supports this with an argument: if we judged by future knowledge, then a person who currently denies Allah but is known to die a believer would be called a believer now, and a person who currently affirms but is known to die a disbeliever would be called a disbeliever now—this is absurd because realities are judged by their present existence, not by what they will become. He illustrates with the example of life and death: Allah knows a living person as living, not as dead at present, even though He knows he will die. Likewise for all attributes. Further, he argues that if matters were judged by their end results, we would have to say we are now in the Hereafter (since that is the final state) and every dead person was alive—which is absurd. This reductio ad absurdum shows the doctrine's falsehood. Then Nasafi addresses an objection: 'Doesn't divine knowledge of the final state make a person a friend or enemy of Allah now?' He answers that friendship (wilāya) and enmity (ʿadāwa) are consequential states arising from faith and disbelief; they can change when faith or disbelief changes. The change occurs on the person (who is described by these), not on the relationship itself—just as knowledge and the known, and informing and what is informed about, are distinct. The passage concludes with 'Allah grants success.' Overall, it is a rational argument maintaining that present reality, not future knowledge, determines current judgment of faith and disbelief.

Key Terms
التصديق
التكذيب
العاقبة
العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine foreknowledge of a person's final state makes them a believer or disbeliever in the present regardless of their current actions.
Correction: Nasafi argues that present attributes are determined by present existence, not by future knowledge. A person is a believer now only if they currently have faith, even if Allah knows they will later disbelieve.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi reject the view that faith is judged by the final outcome (al-ʿāqiba)?
A) Because divine knowledge is not decisive about future states.
B) Because realities are determined by their present existence, not by future knowledge.
C) Because everyone will eventually be a believer.
D) Because the Ash'ari view is based on weak hadith.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi uses reductio ad absurdum to show that judging faith by final outcome is false because it leads to absurd consequences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live your faith today as if your final outcome is already written in stone, or do you strive each moment as if your present affirmation truly defines you before Allah? Are you complacent, assuming a good ending guarantees your current state?
?
When you look at someone sinning openly, do you secretly judge them as 'disbelievers' because you assume a bad end, forgetting that present denial is what makes them disbelievers now—and that repentance could change everything? How does this lesson rebuke your heart?
?
Imagine you knew you would die as a disbeliever—would that make your current acts of worship worthless? Or does the fact that you are now affirming Allah make you truly a believer right now? Are you grateful for your present faith, or do you take it for granted, relying on a future assumption?

Objection and Answer: Divine Knowledge and Friendship/Enmity
Nasafi answers the objection about divine knowledge and present friendship/enmity by clarifying that these are contingent on actual faith and disbelief, not on future knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi responds to the objection that divine foreknowledge of the final state implies present friendship or enmity with Allah.

Core Idea
Friendship and enmity change with faith; divine knowledge does not alter the present relationship.

After his main refutation, Nasafi anticipates an objection: if Allah knows someone will be sealed with faith, does that not make them His friend now? And if He knows someone will be sealed with disbelief, do they not become His enemy now? Nasafi answers by distinguishing between the relationship that results from faith and the capacity for change.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objectors argue that divine knowledge of final state makes a person a friend or enemy of Allah in the present. Identify their reasoning.
They believe that because Allah knows the outcome, the person is currently in that state.
2
Understand the answer
Nasafi responds that friendship and enmity are consequences of faith and disbelief. They change when faith or disbelief changes. So a believer who later disbelieves becomes an enemy. The change occurs on the person, not on the relationship itself.
He distinguishes between the attribute (wilāya) and the person described by it.
3
Apply the analogy
Nasafi compares this to knowledge and the known: knowledge changes according to the state of the known object, but the known object itself changes. Similarly, the person changes, but the relationship of friendship/enmity is derived from their state.
This analogy reinforces his point.

The Invalidity of Saying 'I Am a Believer if Allah Wills'
Nasafi refutes the practice of qualifying 'I am a believer' with 'if Allah wills', using analogy and logical argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the statement 'I am a believer if Allah wills' is invalid when faith is already present, and how Nasafi refutes this practice using analogy and logical consistency.

Core Idea
When faith is actual in the heart, qualifying it with 'if Allah wills' is as false as saying 'I am standing if Allah wills' while standing.

This lesson examines a subtle but important issue in Islamic theology: the practice of suspending one's declaration of faith with the phrase 'if Allah wills.' Nasafi argues that this practice is fundamentally flawed because faith, being internal affirmation (tasdiq), is already a present reality for the believer. The condition implies doubt, which contradicts the certainty of faith. By the end of this lesson, you will see how Nasafi uses a powerful analogy to expose the logical inconsistency in this statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Focus on Nasafi's main claim and his analogy.
Notice the phrase 'لما وجد' which emphasizes the existence of faith.
2
Identify the core analogy
Nasafi compares saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' to saying 'I am standing if Allah wills' while actually standing. Understand why he considers this false.
The condition 'if Allah wills' implies uncertainty about the present state, which is contradictory when the state is certain.
3
Understand the two nuanced positions refuted
Nasafi addresses two groups: those who say 'my faith is true without exception' yet say 'if Allah wills', and those who say 'I am a believer in Allah without exception' yet say 'I am a believer before Allah if Allah wills'. He shows both are meaningless.
4
Reflect on the certainty of faith
Consider why Nasafi insists on affirming faith without condition. How does this protect the certainty of iman?
This connects to the Maturidi position that faith is definitive, not probabilistic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبمعرفة هذا نعرف بطلان مقالتهم أنا لا نقول نحن مؤمنون على الثبات بل نقول نحن مؤمنون إن شاء الله تعالى لأن التصديق لما وجد، فقد وجد الإيمان بحقيقة، فقول من يقول : أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله مع وجود حقيقة التصديق كقول من يقول : أنا قائم إن شاء الله وأنا قاعد إن شاء الله مع وجود حقيقة ذلك، وذلك باطل، ولا معنى لقول من قال منهم إيماني حق بلا استثناء وإذا وصف نفسه مؤمن إن شاء الله، لأن إيمانه إذا كان حقا كان هو مؤمنًا حقيقة كالقعود متى كان متحققا كان الرجل قاعدًا، ولا معنى أيضا لقول من يقول: أنا مؤمن بالله من غير استثناء، وقال أنا مؤمن عند الله إن شاء الله؛ لأن الإيمان إذا تحقق بحقيقته قال: أنا
And by knowing this, we know the falsity of their statement: 'We do not say we are believers steadfastly, but we say we are believers if Allah wills.' Because when affirmation (tasdiq) exists, then faith has existed in reality. So the statement of one who says 'I am a believer if Allah wills' while the reality of affirmation exists is like the statement of one who says 'I am standing if Allah wills' and 'I am sitting if Allah wills' while the reality of that exists. That is false. And there is no meaning to the statement of those among them who say 'My faith is true without exception' while describing himself as 'a believer if Allah wills', because if his faith is true, then he is truly a believer, just as when sitting is actualized the man is sitting. And there is also no meaning to the statement of one who says 'I am a believer in Allah without exception' and says 'I am a believer before Allah if Allah wills'; because when faith is actualized in its reality, he says 'I am'.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the practice of saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' (istithna') when one actually possesses faith. Nasafi begins by linking this discussion to the previous refutation: by knowing the falsity of the muwafat theory, we also know the falsity of this statement. The argument is straightforward: since internal affirmation (tasdiq) is the reality of faith, and it exists in the believer, then faith is actualized. To say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' while affirmation is present is like saying 'I am standing if Allah wills' while one is actually standing. Such a statement is false because it qualifies a present reality with a condition that implies doubt about its existence. Nasafi then addresses a possible nuance: some may say 'my faith is true without exception' yet also say 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' He says this is meaningless because if faith is true, the person is truly a believer, just as if sitting is actualized, the person is truly sitting. He also rejects the position of those who say 'I am a believer in Allah without exception' but then say 'I am a believer before Allah if Allah wills' (implying that the certainty is about eschatological acceptance). He asserts that when faith is actualized in its reality, one should simply affirm it without qualification. The passage cuts off with 'he says: I am' but the point is clear: the proper response is to affirm faith directly, not with istithna'. Nasafi is consistent with the Maturidi position that faith is certain and should not be suspended by conditional language.

Key Terms
الاستثناء
المشيئة
الإيمان
التصديق
الحقيقة
الثبات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' is a sign of humility and is permissible.
Correction: Nasafi proves that this statement is false because it introduces doubt about a present reality. True humility does not require denying certainty in what Allah has granted.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why is saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' invalid?
A) Because it implies that faith is not present.
B) Because it is like saying 'I am standing if Allah wills' while actually standing.
C) Because it denies divine power over future outcomes.
D) Because it is a bid'ah innovation.

Key Takeaway
The statement 'I am a believer if Allah wills' is invalid because faith is a present reality, and such conditionality implies doubt, contradicting the certainty of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself saying 'if Allah wills' about something you are certain of in your heart, like your faith? What does that reveal about your level of certainty? How will you correct that today?
?
When you declare your faith, do you do so with the same certainty as the companions did, or does a lingering doubt prevent you from affirming it unconditionally? What step will you take to strengthen that certainty?
?
Nasafi says that saying 'if Allah wills' about present faith is like saying 'I am standing if Allah wills' while standing. Are there areas in your life where you act as if your faith is conditional? Ask yourself: do I live as though my faith is real and present, or do I hold back due to fear or lack of conviction? What is one thing you will do this week to affirm your faith without reservation?

The Invalidity of 'If Allah Wills' in Iman
Refutes istithna in Iman using analogy and logical arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' contradicts the reality of present Iman.

Core Idea
Present Iman is a reality; attaching a condition to it is logically invalid.

Many Muslims say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' out of humility. But Imam al-Nasafi explains that this statement is invalid because Iman, being inner affirmation (tasdiq), already exists within the believer. To attach a condition to it is like saying 'I am sitting if Allah wills' while sitting — a logical contradiction. In this lesson, we will examine the core argument and the rebuttals to common objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Look for the main claim about the invalidity of istithna.
2
Identify the analogy
Notice how the author compares saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' to saying 'I am standing if Allah wills' while standing. What is the point of this comparison?
The analogy shows that a condition on an already existent quality is meaningless.
3
Understand the rebuttals
The author gives three rebuttals to possible objections. List them: the 'true Iman' objection, the 'without exception' objection, and the 'with Allah' objection.
Each rebuttal reinforces that present Iman is fully realized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة المشيئة في الإيمان وبمعرفة هذا نعرف بطلان مقالتهم أنا لا نقول نحن مؤمنون على الثبات بل نقول نحن مؤمنون إن شاء الله تعالى لأن التصديق لما وجد، فقد وجد الإيمان بحقيقة، فقول من يقول : أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله مع وجود حقيقة التصديق كقول من يقول : أنا قائم إن شاء الله وأنا قاعد إن شاء الله مع وجود حقيقة ذلك، وذلك باطل، ولا معنى لقول من قال منهم إيماني حق بلا استثناء وإذا وصف نفسه مؤمن إن شاء الله، لأن إيمانه إذا كان حقا كان هو مؤمنًا حقيقة كالقعود متى كان متحققا كان الرجل قاعدًا، ولا معنى أيضا لقول من يقول: أنا مؤمن بالله من غير استثناء، وقال أنا مؤمن عند الله إن شاء الله؛ لأن الإيمان إذا تحقق بحقيقته كان مؤمنا عند الله حقيقة، وإنما الشك أن يكون مؤمنا وقت الموت ولا يظن بهم أنهم يشكون في وجود التصديق منهم للحال بل إنما يثبتون ذلك على القول بالموافاة وهو أن المذهب عندهم أن لا عبرة للإيمان الموجود للحال ولا للكفر الموجود للحال بل العبرة بحالة الموت وتلك الحالة مستورة عليهم، فإذا لم يعلموا بها لا يعلمون ما هم عليه للحال لسقوط اعتبار ما هو الموجود للحال، وبمعرفة بطلان ذلك يعرف بطلان هذا
The issue of will in faith. And by knowing this, we know the invalidity of their statement that we do not say 'we are believers in a constant state' but we say 'we are believers if Allah wills'. Because when tasdiq (affirmation) exists, Iman has truly existed. So the saying of one who says 'I am a believer if Allah wills' while the reality of tasdiq exists is like the saying of one who says 'I am standing if Allah wills' and 'I am sitting if Allah wills' while the reality of that exists, and that is invalid. And there is no meaning to the saying of one who said from them 'my Iman is true without exception' and he describes himself as 'believer if Allah wills', because if his Iman is true, he is truly a believer, just like when sitting is actualized, the man is sitting. And there is also no meaning to the saying of one who says 'I am a believer in Allah without exception' and says 'I am a believer with Allah if Allah wills', because if Iman is actualized by its reality, he is a believer with Allah truly. But the doubt is that he might be a believer at the time of death. And it is not thought of them that they doubt in the existence of tasdiq from them at present. Rather, they affirm that on the view of muwafah (the condition at death), which is that the school of thought with them is that there is no consideration for the Iman existing at present, nor for the kufr existing at present, but the consideration is for the state of death, and that state is hidden from them. So when they do not know it, they do not know what they are upon at present due to the lapse of consideration for what exists at present. And by knowing the invalidity of that, the invalidity of this is known.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that a believer should say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' when asked about his Iman. The author begins by stating that the invalidity of their statement is known by knowing that Iman is the reality of tasdiq. Since tasdiq is already present in the believer, Iman is realized as a reality. Therefore, saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' while tasdiq exists is analogous to saying 'I am standing if Allah wills' while actually standing—it is logically invalid because it attaches a condition to something that already exists. The author then addresses the claim of some that their Iman is true but they still say 'if Allah wills'. The author argues that if Iman is true, then one is truly a believer, just as if one is sitting, he is truly sitting. Then he addresses the claim of those who say 'I am a believer in Allah without exception' yet also say 'I am a believer with Allah if Allah wills', arguing that if Iman is actualized, then one is truly a believer with Allah. The author explains that the doubt is not about present Iman but about the final state at death. The opposing school (the Ash'aris perhaps) holds the view of muwafah, that only the state at death determines whether one is a believer or disbeliever, and that state is hidden. So they do not know their present status because the present Iman is not considered. The author refutes this by showing that if the present Iman is not considered, then the present kufr also would not be considered, leading to absurdity. The passage concludes that knowing the invalidity of that view shows the invalidity of this form of istithna.

Key Terms
تصديق
إيمان
مشيئة
الاستثناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is humble to say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' to avoid self-praise.
Correction: The author shows it is logically invalid because Iman is already present.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the main reason saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' is invalid?
A) It shows lack of humility.
B) It is like saying 'I am standing if Allah wills' while standing.
C) Allah forbids it.
D) It causes doubt in others.

Key Takeaway
Saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' is invalid because it attaches a condition to something that already exists — our present Iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills'? What does that reveal about your certainty in your own faith right now?
?
If your Iman is truly present, why would you hesitate to affirm it absolutely? What fear or doubt holds you back from declaring your faith without condition?
?
After understanding this lesson, will you commit to removing 'if Allah wills' from your affirmation of Iman? How will you remind yourself of the reality of your tasdiq when doubt creeps in?

Refuting the Muwafah View on Iman
Refutes the muwafah view and its consequence of istithna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the muwafah view (that only the state at death matters) leads to the false practice of istithna.

Core Idea
The final state at death is hidden; present Iman is real and should be affirmed.

Some theologians argue that only the state at death determines true belief, making present Iman uncertain. Imam al-Nasafi refutes this by showing that if present Iman is not considered, then present kufr also would not be considered, leading to absurdity. He argues that the doubt about the final state does not justify doubting the reality of present Iman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the muwafah view
Read the passage to understand what the opposing school believes: that only the state at death determines Iman or kufr, not the present state.
2
Understand their reasoning
Because the state at death is hidden, they claim they cannot be sure of their present Iman. They still affirm present tasdiq, but consider it irrelevant.
3
See the refutation
The author argues that if present Iman is not considered, then present kufr would also not be considered, which undermines all religious accountability. Thus, their view is invalid.
The passage ends by stating that knowing the invalidity of muwafah shows the invalidity of their practice of istithna.
